## File: ClassicalInfo/Capacity.lean
```
import ClassicalInfo.Entropy
import Mathlib.Data.Finset.Fin
import Mathlib.Data.Fintype.Fin

--Classical capacity
-- * Define "code"
-- * Define (Shannon) capacity of a (iid, memoryless) channel
-- * Prove Shannon's capacity theorems

variable (A I O : Type*)

/-- Here we define a *Code* by an encdoder and a decoder. The encoder is a function that takes
 strings (`List`s) of any length over an alphabet `A`, and returns strings over `I`;
 the decoder takes `O` and gives back strings over `A`. The idea is that a channel
 would map from strings of `I` to `O`. Important special cases are where `I=O` (the channel doesn't
 change the symbol set), and `FixedLengthCode` where the output lengths only depend on input lengths. -/
structure Code where
  encoder : List A ‚Üí List I
  decoder : List O ‚Üí List A

/-- A `FixedLengthCode` is a `Code` whose output lengths don't depend on the input content, only
 the input length. -/
structure FixedLengthCode extends Code A I O where
  enc_length : ‚Ñï ‚Üí ‚Ñï
  enc_maps_length : ‚àÄ as, (encoder as).length = enc_length (as.length)
  dec_length : ‚Ñï ‚Üí ‚Ñï
  dec_maps_length : ‚àÄ is, (decoder is).length = dec_length (is.length)

/-- A `BlockCode` is a `FixedLengthCode` that (1) maps symbols in discrete blocks of fixed length,
 (2) the encoded alphabet `I` has a canonical injection into `O`, and (3) has encoder and decoders
 that are inverses of each other. This is well-suited to describing noise and erasure channels. If
 the channel merely "corrupts" the data then this `O = I`; the erasure channel might for instance take
 `O = I ‚äï Unit` or `Option I`.

 We define the behavior of a block code to "fail" if the input is not a multiple of the block size,
 by having it return an empty list. -/
structure BlockCode (io : I ‚Üí O) extends FixedLengthCode A I O where
  block_in : ‚Ñï
  block_out : ‚Ñï
  block_enc : (Fin block_in ‚Üí A) ‚Üí (Fin block_out ‚Üí I)
  block_dec : (Fin block_out ‚Üí O) ‚Üí (Fin block_in ‚Üí A)
  block_enc_dec_inv : ‚àÄ as, block_dec (io ‚àò (block_enc as)) = as
  enc_length na := if na % block_in != 0 then 0 else (na / block_in) * block_out
  dec_length no := if no % block_out != 0 then 0 else (no / block_out) * block_in
  encoder as := if as.length % block_in != 0 then [] else
    sorry
  decoder os := if os.length % block_out != 0 then [] else
    sorry
  enc_maps_length := sorry
  dec_maps_length := sorry

```

## File: ClassicalInfo/Channel.lean
```
import ClassicalInfo.Distribution
import Mathlib.MeasureTheory.Measure.MeasureSpaceDef

open BigOperators

/- Channels, as in information theory.

A `Channel` is as a function from `List`s over an input alphabet A to a distribution
of lists over an output alphabet B. The most important case of interest here
is the memoryless channel, which preserves lengths and acts on each symbol
identically and independently.
-/

variable (I O : Type*) [Fintype O]

/- Actually defining Channels this way gets messy fast because of the measure theory.

/-- Although we could simply `def Channel := List A ‚Üí List B`, defining it as
a structure lets us extend this structure by adding additional properties while
staying a `Channel`. -/
structure Channel [MeasurableSpace O] where
  map : List I ‚Üí MeasureTheory.Measure (List O)
  map_prob : ‚àÄis, IsProbabilityMeasure (map is)

namespace Channel

variable (A B C D : Type*)
variable (Cab : Channel A B) (Cbc : Channel B C) (Ccd : Channel C D)

/-- Identity channel -/
def id : Channel A A :=
  ‚ü®_root_.id‚ü©

/-- Composition of two channels -/
def comp : Channel A C :=
  ‚ü®Cbc.map ‚àò Cab.map‚ü©

/-- Product of two channels, acting on two product types in parallel. -/
def product : Channel (A √ó C) (B √ó D) :=
  ‚ü®Cab.map √ó Ccd.map‚ü©
-/

/-- Discrete Memoryless Channel. Each input symbol `I` has a corresponding
 output distribution `Distribution O`, and this process is applied
 independently on each symbol in the list. -/
structure DMChannel where
  symb_dist : I ‚Üí Distribution O

namespace DMChannel

/-- Apply a discrete memoryless channel to an n-character string. -/
def on_fin (C : DMChannel I O) {n : ‚Ñï} (is : Fin n ‚Üí I) : Distribution (Fin n ‚Üí O) :=
  ‚ü®fun os ‚Ü¶ ‚àè k, C.symb_dist (is k) (os k), by
    -- change ‚àë os in Fintype.piFinset fun x => (Finset.univ : Finset O), ‚àè k : Fin n, ((C.symb_dist (is k)) (os k) : ‚Ñù) = 1
    -- have : ‚àÄi, Finset.sum Finset.univ (C.symb_dist i) = 1 :=
    --   fun i ‚Ü¶ Distribution.prop <| C.symb_dist i
    -- rw [Finset.sum_prod_piFinset]
    -- simp [this]
    sorry‚ü©

/-- Apply a discrete memoryless channel to a list. -/
def on_list (C : DMChannel I O) (is : List I) : Distribution (Fin (is.length) ‚Üí O) :=
  C.on_fin is.get

end DMChannel

```

## File: ClassicalInfo/Distribution.lean
```
import ClassicalInfo.Prob

import Mathlib.Analysis.Convex.Combination

/-! # Distributions on finite sets

We define the type `Distribution Œ±` on a `Fintype Œ±`. By restricting ourselves to distributoins on finite types,
a lot of notation and casts are greatly simplified. This suffices for (most) finite-dimensional quantum theory.
-/

noncomputable section
open NNReal
open Classical
open BigOperators

/--
We define our own (discrete) probability distribution notion here, instead
of using `PMF` from Mathlib, because that uses ENNReals everywhere to maintain compatibility
with `MeasureTheory.Measure`.

The probabilities internal to a Distribution are NNReals. This lets us more easily
write the statement that they sum to 1, since NNReals can be added. (Probabilities,
on their own, cannot.) But the FunLike instance gives `Prob` out, which carry the
information that they are all in the range [0,1].
-/
def Distribution (Œ± : Type u) [Fintype Œ±] : Type u :=
  { f : Œ± ‚Üí Prob // Finset.sum Finset.univ (fun i ‚Ü¶ (f i : ‚Ñù)) = 1 }

namespace Distribution

variable {Œ± Œ≤ : Type*} [Fintype Œ±] [Fintype Œ≤]

/-- Make a distribution, proving only that the values are nonnegative and that the
sum is 1. The fact that the values are at most 1 is derived as a consequence. -/
def mk' (f : Œ± ‚Üí ‚Ñù) (h‚ÇÅ : ‚àÄi, 0 ‚â§ f i) (hN : ‚àë i, f i = 1) : Distribution Œ± :=
  have h‚ÇÉ : ‚àÄx, f x ‚â§ 1 := by
    intro x
    simp [‚Üê hN, Fintype.sum_eq_sum_compl_add x]
    exact Finset.sum_nonneg' h‚ÇÅ
  ‚ü® fun i ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®f i, ‚ü®h‚ÇÅ i, h‚ÇÉ i‚ü©‚ü©, hN‚ü©

instance instFunLikeProb : FunLike (Distribution Œ±) Œ± Prob where
  coe p a := p.1 a
  coe_injective' _ _ h :=
    Subtype.ext <| funext fun v ‚Ü¶ by
      simpa only [Subtype.mk.injEq, coe_inj] using congrFun h v

@[simp]
theorem normalized (d : Distribution Œ±) : Finset.sum Finset.univ (fun i ‚Ü¶ (d i : ‚Ñù)) = 1 :=
  d.2

abbrev prob (d : Distribution Œ±) := (d : Œ± ‚Üí Prob)

@[simp]
theorem fun_eq_val (d : Distribution Œ±) : d.val = d :=
  rfl

@[simp]
theorem funlike_apply (d : Œ± ‚Üí Prob) (h : _) (x : Œ±) :
    DFunLike.coe (self := instFunLikeProb) ‚ü®d, h‚ü© x = d x :=
  rfl

@[ext]
theorem ext {p q : Distribution Œ±} (h : ‚àÄ x, p x = q x) : p = q :=
  DFunLike.ext p q h

/-- A distribution is a witness that d is nonempty. -/
instance nonempty (d : Distribution Œ±) : Nonempty Œ± := by
  by_contra h
  simpa [not_nonempty_iff.mp h] using d.2

/-- Make an constant distribution: supported on a single element. This is also called, variously, a
 "One-point distribution", a "Degenerate distribution", a "Deterministic distribution", a
 "Delta function", or a "Point mass distribution". -/
def constant (x : Œ±) : Distribution Œ± :=
  ‚ü®fun y ‚Ü¶ if x = y then 1 else 0,
    by simp [apply_ite]‚ü©

theorem constant_def (x : Œ±) : (constant x : Œ± ‚Üí Prob) = fun y ‚Ü¶ if x = y then 1 else 0 := by
  rfl

@[simp]
theorem constant_eq (x : Œ±) : constant x y = if x = y then 1 else 0 := by
  rfl

@[simp]
theorem constant_def' (x y : Œ±) : (constant x : Œ± ‚Üí Prob) y = if x = y then 1 else 0 := by
  rw [‚Üê Prob.eq_iff_nnreal]
  change (Prob.toNNReal ‚àò (constant x)) y = (if x = y then 1 else 0 : Prob)
  rw [constant_def x]
  split_ifs with h
  <;> simp [h]

/-- If a distribution has an element with probability 1, the distribution has a constant. -/
theorem constant_of_exists_one {D : Distribution Œ±} {x : Œ±} (h : D x = 1) : D = Distribution.constant x := by
  ext y
  by_cases h‚ÇÇ : x = y
  ¬∑ simp [h, ‚Üê h‚ÇÇ]
  ¬∑ simp only [constant_eq, h‚ÇÇ, ‚ÜìreduceIte, Prob.coe_zero]
    by_contra h‚ÇÉ
    replace h‚ÇÉ : 0 < (D y : ‚Ñù) := by
      linarith (config := {splitNe := true}) only [h‚ÇÉ, @Prob.zero_le_coe (D y)]
    have := D.normalized
    rw [‚Üê Finset.add_sum_erase _ _ (Finset.mem_univ x), h, Prob.coe_one] at this
    rw [‚Üê Finset.add_sum_erase _ _ (a := y) (by simpa using (Ne.symm h‚ÇÇ))] at this
    have : 0 ‚â§ ‚àë x ‚àà Finset.erase (Finset.erase Finset.univ x) y, (D x : ‚Ñù) :=
      Finset.sum_nonneg' (fun _ ‚Ü¶ Prob.zero_le_coe)
    linarith

/-- Make an uniform distribution. -/
def uniform [n : Nonempty Œ±] : Distribution Œ± :=
  ‚ü®fun _ ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®1 / (Finset.univ.card (Œ± := Œ±)), by
    have : 0 < Finset.univ.card (Œ± := Œ±) :=
      Finset.Nonempty.card_pos (Finset.univ_nonempty_iff.mpr n)
    bound‚ü©, by simp‚ü©

@[simp]
theorem uniform_def [Nonempty Œ±] (y : Œ±) : ((uniform y) : ‚Ñù) = 1 / (Finset.univ.card (Œ± := Œ±)) :=
  rfl

/-- Make a distribution on a product of two Fintypes. -/
def prod (d1 : Distribution Œ±) (d2 : Distribution Œ≤) : Distribution (Prod Œ± Œ≤) :=
  ‚ü®fun x ‚Ü¶ (d1 x.1) * (d2 x.2), by
    simp [‚Üê Finset.mul_sum, Fintype.sum_prod_type]‚ü©

@[simp]
theorem prod_def (x : Œ±) (y : Œ≤) : prod d1 d2 ‚ü®x, y‚ü© = (d1 x) * (d2 y) :=
  rfl

/-- Given a distribution on Œ±, extend it to a distribution on `Sum Œ± Œ≤` by giving it no support on `Œ≤`. -/
def extend_right (d : Distribution Œ±) : Distribution (Œ± ‚äï Œ≤) :=
  ‚ü®fun x ‚Ü¶ Sum.casesOn x d.val (Function.const _ 0), by simp‚ü©

/-- Given a distribution on Œ±, extend it to a distribution on `Sum Œ≤ Œ±` by giving it no support on `Œ≤`. -/
def extend_left (d : Distribution Œ±) : Distribution (Œ≤ ‚äï Œ±) :=
  ‚ü®fun x ‚Ü¶ Sum.casesOn x (Function.const _ 0) d.val, by simp‚ü©

/-- Make a convex mixture of two distributions on the same set. -/
instance instMixable : Mixable (Œ± ‚Üí ‚Ñù) (Distribution Œ±) :=
  Mixable.instSubtype (inferInstance) (fun _ _ hab hx hy ‚Ü¶ by
    simp [Mixable.mix_ab, Finset.sum_add_distrib, ‚Üê Finset.mul_sum, hab, hx, hy]
  )

/-- Given a distribution on type Œ± and an equivalence to type Œ≤, get the corresponding
distribution on type Œ≤. -/
def relabel (d : Distribution Œ±) (œÉ : Œ≤ ‚âÉ Œ±) : Distribution Œ≤ :=
  ‚ü®fun b ‚Ü¶ d (œÉ b),
   by rw [Equiv.sum_comp œÉ (fun a ‚Ü¶ (d a : ‚Ñù))]; exact d.prop‚ü©

-- The two properties below (and congrRandVar) follow from the fact that Distribution is a contravariant functor.
-- However, mathlib does not seem to support that outside of the CategoryTheory namespace
/-- Distributions on Œ± and Œ≤ are equivalent for equivalent types Œ± ‚âÉ Œ≤. -/
def congr (œÉ : Œ± ‚âÉ Œ≤) : Distribution Œ± ‚âÉ Distribution Œ≤ := by
  constructor
  case toFun => exact fun d ‚Ü¶ relabel d œÉ.symm
  case invFun => exact fun d ‚Ü¶ relabel d œÉ
  case left_inv =>
    intro d
    ext i
    unfold relabel
    simp only [‚Üê fun_eq_val, Equiv.symm_apply_apply, Subtype.coe_eta]
  case right_inv =>
    intro d
    ext i
    unfold relabel
    simp only [‚Üê fun_eq_val, Equiv.apply_symm_apply, Subtype.coe_eta]

@[simp]
theorem congr_apply (œÉ : Œ± ‚âÉ Œ≤) (d : Distribution Œ±) (j : Œ≤): (congr œÉ d) j = d (œÉ.symm j) := by
  rfl

/-- The inverse and congruence operations for distributions commute -/
@[simp]
theorem congr_symm_apply (œÉ : Œ± ‚âÉ Œ≤) : (Distribution.congr œÉ).symm = Distribution.congr œÉ.symm := by
  rfl

/-- The distribution on Fin 2 corresponding to a coin with probability p. Chance p of 1, 1-p of 0. -/
def coin (p : Prob) : Distribution (Fin 2) :=
  ‚ü®(if ¬∑ = 0 then p else 1 - p), by simp‚ü©

@[simp]
theorem coin_val_zero (p : Prob) : coin p 0 = p := by
  simp [coin]

@[simp]
theorem coin_val_one (p : Prob) : coin p 1 = 1 - p := by
  simp [coin]

/-- Every distribution on two variable is some coin. -/
theorem fin_two_eq_coin (d : Distribution (Fin 2)) : d = coin (d 0) := by
  ext i
  fin_cases i
  ¬∑ simp [coin]
  ¬∑ simpa only [coin, Fin.mk_one, funlike_apply, one_ne_zero, ‚ÜìreduceIte,
    Prob.coe_one_minus, Subtype.eq_iff, Prob.coe_one_minus, eq_sub_iff_add_eq, add_comm,
        fun_eq_val, Fin.sum_univ_two] using d.property

theorem coin_eq_iff (p : Prob) (f : Distribution (Fin 2)) :
    Distribution.coin p = f ‚Üî p = f 0 := by
  constructor
  ¬∑ rintro rfl
    rfl
  ¬∑ rintro rfl
    rw [‚Üê Distribution.fin_two_eq_coin f]

section randvar

/-- A `T`-valued random variable over `Œ±` is a map `var : Œ± ‚Üí T` along
with a probability distribution `distr : Distribution Œ±`. -/
structure RandVar (Œ± : Type*) [Fintype Œ±] (T : Type*) where
  var : Œ± ‚Üí T
  distr : Distribution Œ±

instance instFunctor : Functor (RandVar Œ±) where map f e := ‚ü®f ‚àò e.1, e.2‚ü©

instance instLawfulFunctor : LawfulFunctor (RandVar Œ±) where
  map_const {Œ±} {Œ≤} := by rfl
  id_map _ := by rfl
  comp_map _ _ _ := by rfl

-- `U` is required to be a group just because mix below uses Convex.sum_mem,
-- but it should be provable with just `AddCommMonoid U`
variable {T U : Type*} [AddCommGroup U] [Module ‚Ñù U] [inst : Mixable U T]

/-- `Distribution.exp_val` is the expectation value of a random variable `X`. Under the hood,
it is the "convex combination over a finite family" on the type `T`, afforded by the `Mixable` instance,
with the probability distribution of `X` as weights. -/
def expect_val (X : RandVar Œ± T) : T := by
  let u : U := ‚àë i ‚àà Finset.univ, (X.distr i : ‚Ñù) ‚Ä¢ (inst.to_U (X.var i))
  have ht : ‚àÉ t : T, inst.to_U t = u := by
    have h‚ÇÄ : ‚àÄ i ‚àà Finset.univ, 0 ‚â§ ‚Üë(X.distr i) := by simp
    have h‚ÇÅ : ‚àë i ‚àà Finset.univ, (X.distr i : ‚Ñù) = 1 := by simp
    have hz : ‚àÄ i ‚àà Finset.univ, inst.to_U (X.var i) ‚àà Set.range inst.to_U := by simp [Finset.mem_univ]
    exact Set.mem_range.mp (inst.convex.sum_mem h‚ÇÄ h‚ÇÅ hz)
  exact (inst.mkT ht).1

/-- The expectation value of a random variable over `Œ± = Fin 2` is the same as `Mixable.mix`
with probabiliy weight `X.distr 0` -/
theorem expect_val_eq_mixable_mix (d : Distribution (Fin 2)) (x‚ÇÅ x‚ÇÇ : T) : expect_val ‚ü®![x‚ÇÅ, x‚ÇÇ], d‚ü© = Mixable.mix (d 0) x‚ÇÅ x‚ÇÇ := by
  apply Mixable.to_U_inj
  simp only [Mixable.mix, expect_val, DFunLike.coe, Mixable.to_U_of_mkT]
  calc
    ‚àë i : Fin (Nat.succ 0).succ, (d i : ‚Ñù) ‚Ä¢ Mixable.to_U (![x‚ÇÅ, x‚ÇÇ] i) = ‚àë i, (d i : ‚Ñù) ‚Ä¢ Mixable.to_U (![x‚ÇÅ, x‚ÇÇ] i) := by
      simp
    _ = (d 0 : ‚Ñù) ‚Ä¢ Mixable.to_U (![x‚ÇÅ, x‚ÇÇ] 0) + (d 1 : ‚Ñù) ‚Ä¢ Mixable.to_U (![x‚ÇÅ, x‚ÇÇ] 1) := by
      simp
    _ = (d 0 : ‚Ñù) ‚Ä¢ Mixable.to_U x‚ÇÅ + (1 - d 0).val ‚Ä¢ Mixable.to_U x‚ÇÇ := by
      congr
      simpa only [Subtype.eq_iff, Prob.coe_one_minus, eq_sub_iff_add_eq, add_comm,
        fun_eq_val, Fin.sum_univ_two] using d.property

/-- The expectation value of a random variable with constant probability distribution `constant x` is its value at `x` -/
theorem expect_val_constant (x : Œ±) (f : Œ± ‚Üí T) : expect_val ‚ü®f, (constant x)‚ü© = f x := by
  apply Mixable.to_U_inj
  simp only [expect_val, constant, DFunLike.coe, Mixable.to_U_of_mkT, apply_ite, Prob.coe_one,
    Prob.coe_zero, ite_smul, one_smul, zero_smul, Finset.sum_ite_eq, Finset.mem_univ, ‚ÜìreduceIte]

/-- The expectation value of a nonnegative real random variable is also nonnegative -/
theorem zero_le_expect_val (d : Distribution Œ±) (f : Œ± ‚Üí ‚Ñù) (hpos : 0 ‚â§ f) : 0 ‚â§ expect_val ‚ü®f, d‚ü© := by
  simp only [expect_val, Mixable.mkT, Mixable.to_U, id]
  apply Fintype.sum_nonneg
  intro x
  specialize hpos x
  exact mul_nonneg Prob.zero_le_coe hpos

/-- `T`-valued random variables on `Œ±` and `Œ≤` are equivalent if `Œ± ‚âÉ Œ≤` -/
def congrRandVar (œÉ : Œ± ‚âÉ Œ≤) : RandVar Œ± T ‚âÉ RandVar Œ≤ T := by
  constructor
  case toFun => exact fun X ‚Ü¶ { var := X.var ‚àò œÉ.symm, distr := Distribution.congr œÉ X.distr }
  case invFun => exact fun X ‚Ü¶ { var := X.var ‚àò œÉ, distr := Distribution.congr œÉ.symm X.distr }
  case left_inv =>
    intro e
    dsimp
    congr
    ¬∑ simp [Function.comp_assoc]
    ¬∑ rw [‚Üê Distribution.congr_symm_apply, Equiv.symm_apply_apply]
  case right_inv =>
    intro e
    dsimp
    congr
    ¬∑ simp [Function.comp_assoc]
    ¬∑ rw [‚Üê Distribution.congr_symm_apply, Equiv.apply_symm_apply]

/-- Given a `T`-valued random variable `X` over `Œ±`, mapping over `T` commutes with the equivalence over `Œ±` -/
def map_congr_eq_congr_map {S : Type _} [Mixable U S] (f : T ‚Üí S) (œÉ : Œ± ‚âÉ Œ≤) (X : RandVar Œ± T) :
  f <$> congrRandVar œÉ X = congrRandVar œÉ (f <$> X) := by rfl

/-- The expectation value is invariant under equivalence of random variables -/
@[simp]
theorem expect_val_congr_eq_expect_val (œÉ : Œ± ‚âÉ Œ≤) (X : RandVar Œ± T) : expect_val (congrRandVar œÉ X) = expect_val X := by
  apply Mixable.to_U_inj
  simp only [expect_val, congrRandVar, Equiv.coe_fn_mk, Function.comp_apply, Mixable.to_U_of_mkT,
    congr_apply]
  rw [Equiv.sum_comp œÉ.symm (fun i : Œ± ‚Ü¶ (X.distr i : ‚Ñù) ‚Ä¢ Mixable.to_U (X.var i))]

end randvar

end Distribution

```

## File: ClassicalInfo/Entropy.lean
```
import ClassicalInfo.Distribution
import Mathlib.Analysis.SpecialFunctions.Log.NegMulLog
import Mathlib.Analysis.SpecialFunctions.BinaryEntropy
import ClassicalInfo.ForMathlib.Analysis.SpecialFunctions.Log.NegMulLog

/-! # Shannon entropy

Definitions and facts about the Shannon entropy function -x*ln(x), both on a single
variable and on a distribution.

There is significant overlap with `Real.negMulLog` and `Real.binEntropy` in Mathlib,
and probably these files could be combined in some form. -/

noncomputable section
open NNReal

variable {Œ± : Type u} [Fintype Œ±]

/-- The one-event entropy function, H‚ÇÅ(p) = -p*ln(p). Uses nits. -/
def H‚ÇÅ : Prob ‚Üí ‚Ñù :=
  fun x ‚Ü¶ Real.negMulLog x

/-- H‚ÇÅ of 0 is zero.-/
@[simp]
def H‚ÇÅ_zero_eq_zero : H‚ÇÅ 0 = 0 := by
  simp [H‚ÇÅ]

/-- H‚ÇÅ of 1 is zero.-/
@[simp]
def H‚ÇÅ_one_eq_zero : H‚ÇÅ 1 = 0 := by
  simp [H‚ÇÅ]

/-- Entropy is nonnegative. -/
theorem H‚ÇÅ_nonneg (p : Prob) : 0 ‚â§ H‚ÇÅ p := by
  rw [H‚ÇÅ, Real.negMulLog, neg_mul, Left.nonneg_neg_iff]
  exact Real.mul_log_nonpos p.zero_le_coe p.coe_le_one

/-- Entropy is less than 1. -/
theorem H‚ÇÅ_le_1 (p : Prob) : H‚ÇÅ p < 1 := by
  rw [H‚ÇÅ]
  by_cases h : p = 0
  ¬∑ norm_num [h]
  ¬∑ have hp0 : 0 < p := lt_of_le_of_ne' p.zero_le h
    have h‚ÇÇ := Real.abs_log_mul_self_lt p hp0 p.coe_le_one
    rw [mul_comm, ‚Üê abs_neg, ‚Üê neg_mul] at h‚ÇÇ
    exact lt_of_abs_lt h‚ÇÇ

/-- Entropy is at most 1/e. -/
theorem H‚ÇÅ_le_exp_m1 (p : Prob) : H‚ÇÅ p ‚â§ Real.exp (-1) :=
  Real.negMulLog_le_rexp_neg_one p.zero_le_coe

theorem H‚ÇÅ_concave : ‚àÄ (x y : Prob), ‚àÄ (p : Prob), p[H‚ÇÅ x ‚Üî H‚ÇÅ y] ‚â§ H‚ÇÅ (p[x ‚Üî y]) := by
  intros x y p
  simp only [H‚ÇÅ, smul_eq_mul, Prob.coe_one_minus, Mixable.mix, Mixable.mix_ab, Mixable.mkT_instUniv,
    Prob.mkT_mixable, Prob.to_U_mixable, Mixable.to_U_instUniv, Prob.to_U_mixable]
  by_cases hxy : x = y
  ¬∑ subst hxy
    ring_nf
    exact le_refl _
  by_cases hp : (p:‚Ñù) = 0
  ¬∑ norm_num [hp]
  by_cases hp‚ÇÅ : (p:‚Ñù) = 1
  ¬∑ norm_num [hp‚ÇÅ]
  rw [‚Üê ne_eq] at hxy hp hp‚ÇÅ
  have := Real.strictConcaveOn_negMulLog.2
  replace := @this x ?_ y ?_ ?_ p (1 - p) ?_ ?_ (by linarith)
  ¬∑ simp only [smul_eq_mul] at this
    apply le_of_lt
    convert this
  ¬∑ simp only [Set.mem_Ici, Prob.zero_le_coe]
  ¬∑ simp only [Set.mem_Ici, Prob.zero_le_coe]
  ¬∑ simpa only [Prob.ne_iff]
  ¬∑ exact lt_of_le_of_ne p.zero_le_coe hp.symm
  ¬∑ linarith (config := {splitNe := true}) [p.coe_le_one]

/-- The Shannon entropy of a discrete distribution, H(X) = ‚àë H‚ÇÅ(p_x). -/
def H‚Çõ (d : Distribution Œ±) : ‚Ñù :=
  Finset.sum Finset.univ (fun x ‚Ü¶ H‚ÇÅ (d.prob x))

/-- Shannon entropy of a distribution is nonnegative. -/
theorem H‚Çõ_nonneg (d : Distribution Œ±) : 0 ‚â§ H‚Çõ d :=
  Finset.sum_nonneg' fun _ ‚Ü¶ H‚ÇÅ_nonneg _

/-- Shannon entropy of a distribution is at most ln d. -/
theorem H‚Çõ_le_log_d (d : Distribution Œ±) : H‚Çõ d ‚â§ Real.log (Fintype.card Œ±) := by
  --Thanks Aristotle
  by_cases h : Fintype.card Œ± = 0
  ¬∑ simp_all [H‚Çõ, Fintype.card_eq_zero_iff.mp h]
  -- Since the sum of the probabilities is 1, we can apply Jensen's inequality for the convex function -x log x.
  have h_jensen {p : Œ± ‚Üí ‚Ñù} (hsum : ‚àë i, p i = 1) (hp : ‚àÄ i, 0 ‚â§ p i ‚àß p i ‚â§ 1) :
      -‚àë i, p i * (p i).log ‚â§ Real.log (Fintype.card Œ±) := by
    have h_jensen : (‚àë i, (Fintype.card Œ± : ‚Ñù)‚Åª¬π * p i) * (‚àë i, (Fintype.card Œ± : ‚Ñù)‚Åª¬π * p i).log ‚â§
          (‚àë i, (Fintype.card Œ± : ‚Ñù)‚Åª¬π * (p i * (p i).log)) := by
      have h_convex : ConvexOn ‚Ñù (Set.Icc 0 1) (fun x ‚Ü¶ x * Real.log x) :=
        Real.convexOn_mul_log.subset Set.Icc_subset_Ici_self (convex_Icc 0 1)
      convert h_convex.map_sum_le _ _ _ <;> aesop
    simp_rw [‚Üê Finset.mul_sum, hsum, mul_one, Real.log_inv] at h_jensen
    have : 0 < (Fintype.card Œ± : ‚Ñù)‚Åª¬π := by positivity
    have := mul_inv_cancel‚ÇÄ <| show (Fintype.card Œ± : ‚Ñù) ‚â† 0 by positivity
    nlinarith
  simpa [H‚Çõ, H‚ÇÅ, Real.negMulLog] using h_jensen d.2 (by grind)

/-- The shannon entropy of a constant variable is zero. -/
@[simp]
theorem H‚Çõ_constant_eq_zero {i : Œ±} : H‚Çõ (Distribution.constant i) = 0 := by
  simp [H‚Çõ, apply_ite]

/-- Shannon entropy of a uniform distribution is ln d. -/
theorem H‚Çõ_uniform [Nonempty Œ±] :
    H‚Çõ (Distribution.uniform (Œ± := Œ±)) = Real.log (Finset.univ.card (Œ± := Œ±)) := by
  simp [H‚Çõ, Distribution.prob, H‚ÇÅ, Real.negMulLog]

/-- Shannon entropy of two-event distribution. -/
theorem H‚Çõ_coin (p : Prob) : H‚Çõ (Distribution.coin p) = Real.binEntropy p := by
  simp [H‚Çõ, H‚ÇÅ, Distribution.coin, Real.binEntropy_eq_negMulLog_add_negMulLog_one_sub]

--TODO:
-- * Shannon entropy is concave under mixing distributions.
-- * Shannon entropy as an expectation value

```

import Mathlib.Analysis.SpecialFunctions.Log.NegMulLog

noncomputable section
open NNReal

namespace Real

theorem negMulLog_strictMonoOn : StrictMonoOn Real.negMulLog (Set.Icc 0 (exp (-1))) := by
  apply strictMonoOn_of_deriv_pos
  ¬∑ exact convex_Icc 0 (exp (-1))
  ¬∑ exact continuous_negMulLog.continuousOn
  ¬∑ intro x hx
    rw [interior_Icc, Set.mem_Ioo] at hx
    linarith only [log_exp (-1), log_lt_log hx.left hx.right, deriv_negMulLog hx.left.ne']

theorem negMulLog_strictAntiOn : StrictAntiOn Real.negMulLog (Set.Ici (exp (-1))) := by
  apply strictAntiOn_of_deriv_neg
  ¬∑ exact convex_Ici (exp (-1))
  ¬∑ exact continuous_negMulLog.continuousOn
  ¬∑ intro x hx
    rw [interior_Ici' Set.nonempty_Iio, Set.mem_Ioi] at hx
    have hx' : x ‚â† 0 := by grind [exp_nonneg]
    linarith [log_exp (-1), log_lt_log (exp_pos (-1)) hx, deriv_negMulLog hx']

theorem negMulLog_le_rexp_neg_one {x : ‚Ñù} (hx : 0 ‚â§ x) : negMulLog x ‚â§ exp (-1) := by
  by_cases hp : x < exp (-1)
  ¬∑ grw [negMulLog_strictMonoOn.monotoneOn (by grind) (by grind) hp.le]
    simp [negMulLog]
  by_cases hp' : Real.exp (-1) < x
  ¬∑ grw [negMulLog_strictAntiOn.antitoneOn (by grind) (by grind) hp'.le]
    simp [negMulLog]
  ¬∑ simp [show x = exp (-1) by order, negMulLog]

end Real

import Mathlib.Analysis.Convex.Mul
import Mathlib.Analysis.SpecialFunctions.Log.Basic
import Mathlib.Analysis.SpecialFunctions.Log.ENNRealLog
import Mathlib.Data.NNReal.Basic
import Mathlib.Data.EReal.Basic

/-! # Probabilities

This defines a type `Prob`, which is simply any real number in the interval O to 1. This then comes with
additional statements such as its application to convex sets, and it makes useful type alias for
functions that only make sense on probabilities.

A significant application is in the `Mixable` typeclass, also in this file, which is a general notion
of convex combination that applies to types as opposed to sets; elements are `Mixable.mix`ed using `Prob`s.
-/

noncomputable section
open NNReal
open Classical

/-- `Prob` is a real number in the interval [0,1]. Similar to NNReal in many definitions, but this
  allows other nice things more 'safely' such as convex combination. -/
@[reducible]
def Prob := { p : ‚Ñù // 0 ‚â§ p ‚àß p ‚â§ 1 }

namespace Prob

instance : Coe Prob ‚Ñù := ‚ü®Subtype.val‚ü©

instance canLift : CanLift ‚Ñù Prob Subtype.val fun r => 0 ‚â§ r ‚àß r ‚â§ 1 :=
  Subtype.canLift _

instance instZero : Zero Prob :=
  ‚ü®0, by simp‚ü©

instance instOne : One Prob :=
  ‚ü®1, by simp‚ü©

instance instMul : Mul Prob :=
  ‚ü®fun x y ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®x.1 * y.1,
    ‚ü®mul_nonneg x.2.1 y.2.1, mul_le_one‚ÇÄ x.2.2 y.2.1 y.2.2‚ü©‚ü©‚ü©

@[simp, norm_cast]
theorem coe_zero : (0 : Prob).val = 0 :=
  rfl

@[simp, norm_cast]
theorem coe_one : (1 : Prob).val = 1 :=
  rfl

@[simp, norm_cast]
theorem coe_mul (x y : Prob) : (x * y).val = x.val * y.val :=
  rfl

@[simp, norm_cast]
theorem coe_inf (x y : Prob) : (x ‚äì y).val = x.val ‚äì y.val :=
  rfl

@[simp, norm_cast]
theorem coe_sup (x y : Prob) : (x ‚äî y).val = x.val ‚äî y.val :=
  rfl

instance instCommMonoidWithZero : CommMonoidWithZero Prob where
  mul_assoc := by intros; ext; simp [mul_assoc]
  one_mul := by intros; ext; simp
  mul_one := by intros; ext; simp
  mul_comm := by intros; ext; simp [mul_comm]
  mul_zero := by intros; ext; simp
  zero_mul := by intros; ext; simp

instance instDenselyOrdered : DenselyOrdered Prob :=
  show DenselyOrdered (Set.Icc 0 1) from Set.instDenselyOrdered

instance instCompleteLinearOrder : CompleteLinearOrder Prob :=
  instCompleteLinearOrderElemIccOfFactLe

instance instInhabited : Inhabited Prob where
  default := 0

instance : LinearOrderedCommMonoidWithZero Prob where
  mul_le_mul_left := by
    intros a b h c
    rw [‚Üê Subtype.coe_le_coe]
    exact mul_le_mul_of_nonneg_left h c.2.1
  zero_le_one := (0 : Prob).2.2

@[simp]
theorem zero_le_coe {p : Prob} : 0 ‚â§ (p : ‚Ñù) :=
  p.2.1

@[simp]
theorem coe_le_one {p : Prob} : (p : ‚Ñù) ‚â§ 1 :=
  p.2.2

@[simp]
theorem zero_le {p : Prob} : 0 ‚â§ p :=
  zero_le_coe

@[simp]
theorem le_one {p : Prob} : p ‚â§ 1 :=
  coe_le_one

@[ext] protected theorem eq {n m : Prob} : (n : ‚Ñù) = (m : ‚Ñù) ‚Üí n = m :=
  Subtype.eq

theorem ne_iff {x y : Prob} : (x : ‚Ñù) ‚â† (y : ‚Ñù) ‚Üî x ‚â† y :=
  not_congr <| Prob.eq_iff.symm

@[simp, norm_cast]
theorem toReal_mul (x y : Prob) : (x * y : Prob) = (x : ‚Ñù) * (y : ‚Ñù) := by
  simp only [coe_mul]

/-- Coercion `Prob ‚Üí ‚Ñù‚â•0`. -/
@[coe] def toNNReal : Prob ‚Üí ‚Ñù‚â•0 :=
  fun p ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®p.val, zero_le_coe‚ü©

@[simp]
theorem toNNReal_mk : toNNReal { val := x, property := hx} = { val := x, property := hx.1 } :=
  rfl

instance : Coe Prob ‚Ñù‚â•0 := ‚ü®toNNReal‚ü©

instance canLiftNN : CanLift ‚Ñù‚â•0 Prob toNNReal fun r => r ‚â§ 1 :=
  ‚ü®fun x hx ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®‚ü®x, ‚ü®x.2, hx‚ü©‚ü©, rfl‚ü©‚ü©

protected theorem eq_iff_nnreal (n m : Prob) : (n : ‚Ñù‚â•0) = (m : ‚Ñù‚â•0) ‚Üî n = m := by
  obtain ‚ü®n,hn‚ü© := n
  obtain ‚ü®m,hn‚ü© := m
  simp only [toNNReal_mk, Subtype.mk.injEq, NNReal]

@[simp, norm_cast]
theorem toNNReal_zero : (0 : Prob) = (0 : ‚Ñù‚â•0) :=
  rfl

@[simp, norm_cast]
theorem toNNReal_one : (1 : Prob) = (1 : ‚Ñù‚â•0) :=
  rfl

def NNReal.asProb (p : ‚Ñù‚â•0) (hp : p ‚â§ 1) : Prob :=
  ‚ü®p, ‚ü®p.2, hp‚ü©‚ü©

def NNReal.asProb' (p : ‚Ñù‚â•0) (hp : p.1 ‚â§ 1) : Prob :=
  ‚ü®p, ‚ü®p.2, hp‚ü©‚ü©

theorem zero_lt_coe {p : Prob} (hp : p ‚â† 0) : (0 : ‚Ñù) < p :=
  lt_of_le_of_ne' p.zero_le (unitInterval.coe_ne_zero.mpr hp)

/-- Subtract a probability from another. Truncates to zero, so this is often not great
to work with, for the same reason that Nat subtraction is a pain. But, it lets you write
`1 - p`, which is sufficiently useful on its own that this seems worth having. -/
instance instSub : Sub Prob where
  sub p q := ‚ü®(p - q) ‚äî (0 : ‚Ñù), by
    simpa using le_add_of_le_of_nonneg p.2.2 q.2.1
  ‚ü©

theorem coe_sub (p q : Prob) : (p - q : Prob)  = (p.val - q.val) ‚äî (0 : ‚Ñù) := by
  rfl

@[simp, norm_cast]
theorem coe_one_minus (p : Prob) : (1 - p : Prob) = 1 - (p : ‚Ñù) := by
  simp [coe_sub]

theorem add_one_minus (p : Prob) : p.val + (1 - p).val = 1 := by
  simp

@[simp]
theorem one_minus_inv (p : Prob) : 1 - (1 - p) = p := by
  ext
  simp

instance : OrderTopology Prob :=
  orderTopology_of_ordConnected (ht := Set.ordConnected_Icc)

@[simp, norm_cast]
theorem coe_iInf {Œπ : Type*} [Nonempty Œπ] (f : Œπ ‚Üí Prob) : ‚Üë(‚®Ö t, f t) = (‚®Ö t, f t : ‚Ñù) := by
  apply Monotone.map_ciInf_of_continuousAt
  ¬∑ fun_prop
  ¬∑ exact fun _ _ ‚Ü¶ id
  ¬∑ exact OrderBot.bddBelow _

instance : Nontrivial Prob where
  exists_pair_ne := ‚ü®0, 1, by simp [‚Üê Prob.ne_iff]‚ü©

@[simp]
theorem top_eq_one : (‚ä§ : Prob) = 1 := by
  rfl

@[simp]
theorem sub_zero (p : Prob) : p - 0 = p := by
  ext1; simp [coe_sub]

@[fun_prop]
theorem toNNReal_Continuous : Continuous Prob.toNNReal := by
  unfold Prob.toNNReal
  fun_prop

end Prob

/-- A `Mixable T` typeclass instance gives a compact way of talking about the action of probabilities
  for forming linear combinations in convex spaces. The notation `p [ x‚ÇÅ ‚Üî x‚ÇÇ ]` means to take a convex
  combination, equal to `x‚ÇÅ` if `p=1` and to `x‚ÇÇ` if `p=0`.

  Mixable is defined by an "underlying" data type `U` with addition and scalar multiplication, and a
  bijection between the `T` and a convex set of `U`. For instance, in `Mixable (Distribution (Fin n))`,
  `U` is `n`-element vectors (which form the probability simplex, degenerate in one dimension). For
  `QuantumInfo.Finite.MState` density matrices in quantum mechanics, which are PSD matrices of trace 1,
  `U` is the underlying matrix.

  Why not just stick with existing notions of `Convex`? `Convex` requires that the type already forms an
  `AddCommMonoid` and `Module ‚Ñù`. But many types, such as `Distribution`, are not: there is no good notion of
  "multiplying a probability distribution by 0.3" to get another distribution. We can coerce the distribution
  into, say, a vector or a function, but then we are not doing arithmetic with distributions. Accordingly,
  the expression `0.3 * distA + 0.7 * distB` cannot represent a distribution on its own. -/
class Mixable (U : outParam (Type u)) (T : Type v) [AddCommMonoid U] [Module ‚Ñù U] where
  /-- Getter for the underlying data -/
  to_U : T ‚Üí U
  /-- Proof that this getter is injective -/
  to_U_inj : ‚àÄ {T‚ÇÅ T‚ÇÇ}, to_U T‚ÇÅ = to_U T‚ÇÇ ‚Üí T‚ÇÅ = T‚ÇÇ
  /-- Proof that this image is convex -/
  convex : Convex ‚Ñù (Set.range to_U)
  /-- Function to get a T from a proof that U is in the set. -/
  mkT : {u : U} ‚Üí (‚àÉ t, to_U t = u) ‚Üí { t : T // to_U t = u }

namespace Mixable

variable {T U : Type*} [AddCommMonoid U] [Module ‚Ñù U]

@[reducible]
def mix_ab [inst : Mixable U T] {a b : ‚Ñù} (ha : 0 ‚â§ a) (hb : 0 ‚â§ b) (hab : a + b = 1) (x‚ÇÅ x‚ÇÇ : T) : T :=
  inst.mkT <| inst.convex
    (x := to_U x‚ÇÅ) (exists_apply_eq_apply _ _)
    (y := to_U x‚ÇÇ) (exists_apply_eq_apply _ _)
    ha hb hab

/-- `Mixable.mix` represents the notion of "convex combination" on the type `T`, afforded by the `Mixable`
instance. It takes a `Prob`, that is, a `Real` between 0 and 1. For working directly with a Real, use `mix_ab`. -/
def mix [inst : Mixable U T] (p : Prob) (x‚ÇÅ x‚ÇÇ : T) : T :=
  inst.mix_ab p.zero_le_coe (1 - p).zero_le_coe p.add_one_minus x‚ÇÅ x‚ÇÇ

@[simp]
theorem to_U_of_mkT [inst : Mixable U T] (u : U) {h} : inst.to_U (mkT (u := u) h).1 = u :=
  (mkT (u := u) h).2

notation p "[" x‚ÇÅ:80 "‚Üî" x‚ÇÇ "]" => mix p x‚ÇÅ x‚ÇÇ

notation p "[" x‚ÇÅ:80 "‚Üî" x‚ÇÇ ":" M "]" => mix (inst := M) p x‚ÇÅ x‚ÇÇ

@[simp]
theorem mix_zero [inst : Mixable U T] (x‚ÇÅ x‚ÇÇ : T) : (0 : Prob) [ x‚ÇÅ ‚Üî x‚ÇÇ : inst] = x‚ÇÇ := by
  apply inst.to_U_inj
  simp [mix, mix_ab]

/--When T is the whole space, and T is a suitable vector space over ‚Ñù, we get a Mixable instance.-/
instance instUniv [AddCommMonoid T] [Module ‚Ñù T] : Mixable T T where
  to_U := id
  to_U_inj := id
  convex := by
    convert convex_univ
    simp only [Set.range_id]
  mkT := fun _ ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®_, rfl‚ü©

@[simp]
theorem mkT_instUniv [AddCommMonoid T] [Module ‚Ñù T] {t : T} (h : ‚àÉ t', to_U t' = t) : instUniv.mkT h = ‚ü®t, rfl‚ü© :=
  rfl

@[simp]
theorem to_U_instUniv [AddCommMonoid T] [Module ‚Ñù T] {t : T} : instUniv.to_U t = t :=
  rfl

section pi

theorem instPi.lem_1 {D : Type*} {T U : D ‚Üí Type*} [‚àÄi, AddCommMonoid (U i)] [‚àÄ i, Module ‚Ñù (U i)] [inst : ‚àÄi, Mixable (U i) (T i)]
    {u : (i : D) ‚Üí U i} (h : ‚àÉ (t : (i : D) ‚Üí T i), (fun d => to_U (t d)) = u) (d : D) : ‚àÉ (t : T d), to_U t = u d := by
  obtain ‚ü®t, h‚ü© := h
  use t d
  exact congrFun h d

variable {D : Type*} {T U : D ‚Üí Type*} [‚àÄi, AddCommMonoid (U i)] [‚àÄ i, Module ‚Ñù (U i)] [inst : ‚àÄi, Mixable (U i) (T i)] in
/-- Mixable instance on Pi types. -/
instance instPi : Mixable ((i:D) ‚Üí U i) ((i:D) ‚Üí T i) where
  to_U x := fun d ‚Ü¶ (inst d).to_U (x d)
  to_U_inj h := funext fun d ‚Ü¶ (inst d).to_U_inj (congrFun h d)
  mkT := fun {u} h ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®fun d ‚Ü¶ (inst d).mkT (u := u d) (instPi.lem_1 h d),
    by funext d; simp‚ü©
  convex := by
    simp [Convex, StarConvex]
    intro f‚ÇÅ f‚ÇÇ a b ha hb hab
    use fun d ‚Ü¶ (inst d).mix_ab ha hb hab (f‚ÇÅ d) (f‚ÇÇ d)
    funext d
    simp only [to_U_of_mkT, Pi.add_apply, Pi.smul_apply]

@[simp]
theorem val_mkT_instPi (D : Type*) [inst : Mixable U T] {u : D ‚Üí U} (h : ‚àÉ t, to_U t = u) : (instPi.mkT h).val =
    fun d ‚Ü¶ (inst.mkT (instPi.lem_1 h d)).val :=
  rfl

@[simp]
theorem to_U_instPi (D : Type*) [inst : Mixable U T] {t : D ‚Üí T} : (instPi).to_U t = fun d ‚Ü¶ inst.to_U (t d) :=
  rfl

end pi

/-- Mixable instances on subtypes (of other mixable types), assuming that they
 have the correct closure properties. -/
def instSubtype {T : Type*} {P : T ‚Üí Prop} (inst : Mixable U T)
    (h : ‚àÄ{x y:T},
      ‚àÄ‚¶Éa b : ‚Ñù‚¶Ñ, (ha : 0 ‚â§ a) ‚Üí (hb : 0 ‚â§ b) ‚Üí (hab : a + b = 1) ‚Üí
      P x ‚Üí P y ‚Üí P (inst.mix_ab ha hb hab x y))
    : Mixable U { t // P t} where
  to_U x := inst.to_U (x.val)
  to_U_inj h := Subtype.ext (inst.to_U_inj h)
  mkT := fun {u} h ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®by
    have ‚ü®t,hu‚ü© := inst.mkT (u := u) $ h.casesOn fun t h ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®t, h‚ü©
    use t
    have ‚ü®t‚ÇÅ,ht‚ÇÅ‚ü© := h
    exact (inst.to_U_inj $ hu.trans ht‚ÇÅ.symm) ‚ñ∏ t‚ÇÅ.prop,
    by simp only [to_U_of_mkT]‚ü©
  convex := by
    have hi := inst.convex
    simp [Convex, StarConvex] at hi ‚ä¢
    intro x hx y hy a b ha hb hab
    let ‚ü®z, hz‚ü© := hi x y ha hb hab
    refine ‚ü®z, ‚ü®?_, hz‚ü©‚ü©
    convert h ha hb hab hx hy
    apply inst.to_U_inj
    convert hz
    simp only [to_U_of_mkT]

end Mixable

namespace Prob

/-- Probabilities `Prob` themselves are convex. -/
instance instMixable : Mixable ‚Ñù Prob where
  to_U := Subtype.val
  to_U_inj := Prob.eq
  mkT := fun h ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®‚ü®_, Exists.casesOn h fun t ht => ht ‚ñ∏ t.prop‚ü©, rfl‚ü©
  convex := by
    simp [Convex, StarConvex]
    intro x hx0 hx1 y hy0 hy1 a b ha hb hab
    constructor
    ¬∑ positivity
    ¬∑ nlinarith

@[simp]
theorem to_U_mixable [AddCommMonoid T] [SMul ‚Ñù T] (t : Prob) : instMixable.to_U t = t.val :=
  rfl

@[simp]
theorem mkT_mixable (u : ‚Ñù) (h : ‚àÉ t : Prob, Mixable.to_U t = u) : Mixable.mkT h =
    ‚ü®‚ü®u,Exists.casesOn h fun t ht ‚Ü¶ ht ‚ñ∏ t.2‚ü©, rfl‚ü© :=
  rfl

/-- `Prob.mix` is an alias of `Mixable.mix` so it can be accessed from a probability with
dot notation, e.g. `p.mix x y`. -/
abbrev mix [AddCommMonoid U] [Module ‚Ñù U] [inst : Mixable U T] (p : Prob) (x‚ÇÅ x‚ÇÇ : T) := inst.mix p x‚ÇÅ x‚ÇÇ

section negLog
open ENNReal

/-- Map a probability [0,1] to [0,+‚àû] with -log p. Special case that 0 maps to +‚àû (not 0, as Real.log
does). This makes it `Antitone`.
-/
noncomputable def negLog : Prob ‚Üí ENNReal :=
  fun p ‚Ü¶ if p = 0 then ‚àû else .ofNNReal ‚ü®-Real.log p,
    Left.nonneg_neg_iff.mpr (Real.log_nonpos p.2.1 p.2.2)‚ü©

--Note that this is an em-dash `‚Äî` and not a minus `-`, to make the notation work.
scoped notation "‚Äîlog " => negLog

--TODO: Upgrade to `StrictAnti`. Even better: bundle negLog as `Prob ‚âÉo ENNReal·µí·µà`.
theorem negLog_Antitone : Antitone negLog := by
  intro x y h
  dsimp [negLog]
  split_ifs with h‚ÇÅ h‚ÇÇ h‚ÇÇ
  ¬∑ rfl
  ¬∑ subst y
    exfalso
    change x.1 ‚â§ 0 at h
    have : ¬¨(x.1 = 0) := unitInterval.coe_ne_zero.mpr (by assumption)
    have : 0 ‚â§ x.1 := zero_le
    linarith +splitNe
  ¬∑ exact OrderTop.le_top _
  ¬∑ rw [ENNReal.coe_le_coe, ‚Üê NNReal.coe_le_coe, coe_mk, coe_mk, neg_le_neg_iff]
    apply (Real.log_le_log_iff _ _).mpr h
    <;> exact lt_of_le_of_ne zero_le (unitInterval.coe_ne_zero.mpr (by assumption)).symm

@[simp]
theorem negLog_zero : ‚Äîlog (0 : Prob) = ‚ä§ := by
  simp [negLog]

@[simp]
theorem negLog_one : ‚Äîlog 1 = 0 := by
  simp [negLog]

@[simp]
theorem negLog_eq_top_iff {p : Prob} : ‚Äîlog p = ‚ä§ ‚Üî p = 0 := by
  simp [negLog]

theorem negLog_pos_ENNReal {p : Prob} (hp : p ‚â† 0) : ‚Äîlog p = .ofNNReal ‚ü®-Real.log p,
    Left.nonneg_neg_iff.mpr (Real.log_nonpos p.2.1 p.2.2)‚ü© := by
  simp [negLog, hp]

@[simp]
theorem negLog_pos_Real {p : Prob} : (‚Äîlog p).toReal = -Real.log p := by
  rw [negLog]
  split_ifs with hp
  ¬∑ simp [hp]
  ¬∑ simp

theorem le_negLog_of_le_exp {p : Prob} {x : ‚Ñù} (h : p ‚â§ Real.exp (-x)) : ENNReal.ofReal x ‚â§ ‚Äîlog p := by
  by_cases hx : 0 ‚â§ x
  ¬∑ rw [negLog]
    split_ifs with hp
    ¬∑ exact le_top
    ¬∑ replace hp : 0 < p := lt_of_le_of_ne' p.zero_le hp
      rw [le_iff_lt_or_eq] at h
      rcases h with h|h
      ¬∑ apply le_of_lt
        replace h := Real.strictMonoOn_log hp (Real.exp_pos _) h
        rw [Real.log_exp] at h
        rw [‚Üê ENNReal.toReal_lt_toReal ofReal_ne_top coe_ne_top, toReal_ofReal hx]
        simpa using lt_neg_of_lt_neg h
      ¬∑ apply le_of_eq
        rw [‚Üê ENNReal.toReal_eq_toReal ofReal_ne_top coe_ne_top,
          coe_toReal, coe_mk, h, Real.log_exp, neg_neg, toReal_ofReal hx]
  ¬∑ trans 0
    ¬∑ simp only [nonpos_iff_eq_zero, ofReal_eq_zero, le_of_not_ge hx]
    ¬∑ exact _root_.zero_le _

@[aesop (rule_sets := [finiteness]) safe apply]
theorem negLog_ne_top {p : Prob} (hp : 0 < p.val) : ‚Äîlog p ‚â† ‚àû := by
  simpa [negLog] using ne_of_gt hp

theorem negLog_eq_neg_ENNReal_log (p : Prob) : ‚Äîlog p = -ENNReal.log p := by
  rw [negLog]
  split_ifs with hp
  ¬∑ simp [hp]
  ¬∑ rw [log, if_neg, if_neg]
    ¬∑ norm_cast
    ¬∑ finiteness
    ¬∑ rw [Subtype.ext_iff] at hp
      rw [toNNReal, ENNReal.coe_eq_zero]
      exact NNReal.coe_ne_zero.mp hp

theorem negLog_eq_ofReal_neg_log {p : Prob} (hp : 0 < p) :
    ENNReal.ofReal (-Real.log p) = ‚Äîlog p := by
  rcases p with ‚ü®p, p0, p1‚ü©
  rw [negLog]
  split_ifs with h
  ¬∑ simp_all
  ¬∑ exact ENNReal.ofReal_eq_coe_nnreal (neg_nonneg_of_nonpos (Real.log_nonpos p0 p1))

@[simp]
theorem zero_lt_negLog {p : Prob} : 0 < ‚Äîlog p ‚Üî p ‚â† 1 := by
  --This is messy enough it's probably a sign we're missing other simp lemmas
  rw [negLog]
  split_ifs with h
  ¬∑ simp [h]
  constructor <;> intro h‚ÇÇ <;> contrapose! h‚ÇÇ
  ¬∑ simp [h‚ÇÇ]
  simp only [nonpos_iff_eq_zero, ENNReal.coe_eq_zero] at h‚ÇÇ
  rw [Subtype.ext_iff] at h‚ÇÇ
  simp only [NNReal.val_eq_coe, NNReal.coe_zero, neg_eq_zero, Real.log_eq_zero,
    Set.Icc.coe_eq_zero, Set.Icc.coe_eq_one] at h‚ÇÇ
  rcases h‚ÇÇ with h‚ÇÇ|h‚ÇÇ|h‚ÇÇ
  ¬∑ contradiction
  ¬∑ assumption
  ¬∑ linarith [p.zero_le_coe]

@[fun_prop]
theorem Continuous_negLog : Continuous negLog := by
  --Thanks Aristotle
  have h_cont_at_zero : ContinuousAt ‚Äîlog 0 := by
    unfold Prob.negLog
    rw [ContinuousAt, if_pos rfl, ENNReal.tendsto_nhds_top_iff_nnreal]
    intro x
    rw [Metric.eventually_nhds_iff]
    use Real.exp (-x), by positivity
    rintro ‚ü®a, ha0, ha1‚ü© ha'
    rw [Subtype.dist_eq, Set.Icc.coe_zero, dist_zero_right, Real.norm_eq_abs] at ha'
    split_ifs with h; ¬∑ simp
    rw [Subtype.mk_eq_mk, Set.Icc.coe_zero] at h
    simp only [ENNReal.coe_lt_coe, ‚Üê NNReal.coe_lt_coe, NNReal.coe_mk]
    replace ha' := Real.log_lt_log (by positivity) ((le_abs_self _).trans_lt ha')
    simp only [Real.log_exp] at ha'
    linarith
  have h_cont_on_pos : ContinuousOn ‚Äîlog (Set.Ioi 0) := by
    intro p hp
    apply Filter.Tendsto.congr'
    ¬∑ filter_upwards [self_mem_nhdsWithin] with x hx using negLog_eq_ofReal_neg_log hx
    ¬∑ rw [‚Üê negLog_eq_ofReal_neg_log hp]
      apply ENNReal.continuous_ofReal.continuousAt.tendsto.comp
      exact (continuous_subtype_val.continuousWithinAt.tendsto.log hp.ne').neg
  rw [continuous_iff_continuousAt]
  rintro ‚ü®p, ‚ü®_, _‚ü©‚ü©
  rcases lt_trichotomy p 0 with h | rfl | h
  ¬∑ order
  ¬∑ exact h_cont_at_zero
  ¬∑ exact h_cont_on_pos.continuousAt (Ioi_mem_nhds h)

end negLog

end Prob

```

## File: DOC.md
```
# Definitions
This provides an overview of the main `def`s in the project so far -- datastructures, numerical quantities derived from them, and properties about them. Other definitions like casts or typeclass instances are generally omitted.

* A `Prob` is a real number between 0 and 1.
```
def Prob := { p : ‚Ñù // 0 ‚â§ p ‚àß p ‚â§ 1 }
```
* A `Distribution d` on a finite type `d` is a function from `d ‚Üí Prob` that sums to 1.
```
def Distribution (Œ± : Type u) [Fintype Œ±] : Type u :=
  { f : Œ± ‚Üí Prob // Finset.sum Finset.univ (fun i ‚Ü¶ (f i).toReal) = 1 }
```
* A `Bra d` is a normalized, `‚ÑÇ`-valued vector of length `d`. It has notation `„Äàœà‚à£`.
```
structure Bra :=
  vec : d ‚Üí ‚ÑÇ
  normalized' : ‚àë x, ‚Äñvec x‚Äñ^2 =1
```
* A `Ket d` is defined exactly the same, but separately. It is *not* definitionally equal to `Bra d`. This lets us define the "correct" casting notions between the two, with complex conjugation, without the risk of accidentally identifying the entries of one with the other. It has notation `‚à£œà„Äâ`. Kets can be correctly coerces to Bras and vice versa with this notation. Their inner product is `„ÄàŒæ‚Äñœà„Äâ`.
* A mixed state `MState d` is a d-by-d, ‚ÑÇ-valued matrix that is a positive semidefinite and has trace 1.
```
structure MState (d : Type*) [Fintype d] :=
  m : Matrix d d ‚ÑÇ
  pos : m.PosSemidef
  tr : m.trace = 1
```
* Quantum channels are `CPTPMap dIn dOut`, to map states of dimension `dIn` to dimension `dOut`. They are completely positive trace preserving maps. The explicit definition is a bit complicated, see the "Channels & Maps" section below.

* A `POVM X d` is a collection of `X`-indexed PSD d-by-d matrices that sum to 1. It has associated `measure` functions and can be treated as a channel, etc.
```
structure POVM (X : Type*) (d : Type*) [Fintype X] [Fintype d] where
  mats : X ‚Üí Matrix d d ‚ÑÇ
  pos : ‚àÄ x, (mats x).PosSemidef
  normalized : ‚àë x, mats x = (1 : Matrix d d ‚ÑÇ)
```

## Tensor Products
Tensor products are defined on a variety of types. `Œæ ‚äó œà` works for `Ket`s, `œÅ‚ÇÅ ‚äó œÅ‚ÇÇ` works for `MState`s, and `Œõ‚ÇÅ ‚äó Œõ‚ÇÇ` works for `CPTPMap`s. If the original types have `Fintype d‚ÇÅ` and `Fintype d‚ÇÇ`, this produces things on the space `d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ`, aka `Prod d‚ÇÅ d‚ÇÇ`.

This idea of the top-level type being `Prod` is distinguished in many places! For instance, `MState.IsSeparable` takes an `(d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ)`. It then describes precisely whether the state is separable along the bipartition defined by this top-level `Prod` structure. In this sense, all things in the library currently[^1] look only at bipartitions.

What does this mean? Suppose you have a tripartite system `œÅ : MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ √ó d‚ÇÉ)`, which is defined (by the `√ó` notation of `Prod`) to really be `MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó (d‚ÇÇ √ó d‚ÇÉ))`. then `œÅ.IsSeparable` asks whether `œÅ` is separable across the cut between `d‚ÇÅ` and `d‚ÇÇ √ó d‚ÇÉ`. If you instead have a `œÅ' : MState ((d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ) √ó d‚ÇÉ)`, then `œÅ'.IsSeparable` will ask about the cut between `d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ` and `d‚ÇÉ`. If you want to cut `d‚ÇÇ` from the other two, you'll have to shuffle them around with `MState.SWAP` or similar.

As another example, `QConditionalEnt (œÅ : MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ)) ‚Üí ‚Ñù` computes the conditional entropy between two halves of a system, typically written as `S(œÅ·¥¨|œÅ·¥Æ) = S(œÅ·¥¨·¥Æ) - S(œÅ·¥Æ)`. Here it is defined to always take the `d‚ÇÅ` part as system A, the part that is conditioned on the right. To compute the conditional entropy of `d‚ÇÇ` on the `d‚ÇÅ` part, use `QConditionalEnt œÅ.SWAP`.

[^1]: Eventually there should be support for notions of an "n-qubit system", which n is variable; this is needed for notions like "Pauli strings" or "Stabilizer fidelity" - as well as any notions of coding, and thus, capacity. This will probably look like `[Fintype n] [Fintype d] Ket (n ‚Üí d)` for an `n`-particle system of `d`-qudits, or more generally `[Fintype n] [‚àÄi, Fintype d i] Ket ((i:n) ‚Üí d i)` for a heterogeneous combination. 

## States
* `MState.pure (œà : Ket d) : MState d`: Construct a pure mixed state from a ket.
* `MState.traceLeft (œÅ : MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ)) : MState d‚ÇÇ`: Trace out the left half of a bipartite system.
* `MState.traceRight (œÅ : MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ)) : MState d‚ÇÅ`: Trace out the right half of a bipartite system.
* `MState.spectrum (œÅ : MState d) : Distribution d`: The spectrum of eigenvalues of a mixed state, as a distribution (to indicate that they are positive and sum to 1.)
* `MState.IsSeparable (œÅ : MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ)) : Prop`: A proposition indicating whether a state is separable over the given bipartition.
* `MState.purify (œÅ : MState d) : Ket (d √ó d)`: Turn a mixed state into a pure state on a larger Hilbert space. The fact that this traces back down to the input is given by `MState.traceRight_of_purify`, or `MState.purify'` bundles this fact together.
* `MState.ofClassical (dist : Distribution d) : MState d`: View a distribution as a mixed state, embedded in the standard basis.
* `MState.SWAP (œÅ : MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ)) : MState (d‚ÇÇ √ó d‚ÇÅ)`: Exchange the left and right halves of a state.
* `MState.assoc (œÅ : MState ((d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ) √ó d‚ÇÉ)) : MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ √ó d‚ÇÉ)`: Regroup a state's dimensions, moving the canonical bipartition over to the left. Remember that `d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ √ó d‚ÇÉ` is defined as `(d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ) √ó d‚ÇÉ`.
* `MState.assoc' (œÅ : MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ √ó d‚ÇÉ)) : MState ((d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ) √ó d‚ÇÉ)`: Inverse of `MState.asssoc`, as proved in `MState.assoc_assoc'` and `MState.assoc'_assoc`.

## Channels & Maps
We first describe maps between matrices over a ring `R` as generic functions, `f : Matrix A B R ‚Üí Matrix C D R`. These are not necessarily linear. But, given a matrix `M : Matrix (C √ó D) (A √ó B) R`, we can _interpret_ this as a matrix map `f := M.asMatrixMap`. Why this ordering of indices? Because now multiplying matrices is the correct composition of maps, and multiplying a map `M` onto an (appropriately flattened) vector `V` is equivalent to applying `M.asMatrixMap` to the matrix described by `V`.

_Linear_ maps of matrices are described in this way, `Matrix (C √ó D) (A √ó B) R`. Properties such as "trace preserving" or "complete positivity" can apply to both matrix maps and their linear restrictions, and we state one the general one first and then and other using `.asMatrixMap`.

* Trace preservation:
```
def IsTracePreserving (M : Matrix A A R ‚Üí Matrix B B R) : Prop :=
  ‚àÄ (x : Matrix A A R), (M x).trace = x.trace

def Matrix.IsTracePreserving (M : Matrix (B √ó B) (A √ó A) R) : Prop :=
  IsTracePreserving M.asMatrixMap
```
* Positivity:
```
def IsPositiveMatrixMap (M : Matrix A A R ‚Üí Matrix B B R) : Prop :=
  ‚àÄ{x}, x.PosSemidef ‚Üí (M x).PosSemidef

def IsPositiveMap (M : Matrix (B √ó B) (A √ó A) R) : Prop :=
  IsPositiveMatrixMap M.asMatrixMap
```
* Complete positivity: Any Kronecker product with the `n`-fold identity map is still a positive map. This way of stating the definition is unattractive because of how it handles the Kronecker products, and likely to change.
```
def IsCompletelyPositive (M : Matrix (B √ó B) (A √ó A) R) : Prop :=
  ‚àÄ (n : ‚Ñï), IsPositiveMap (matrixMap_kron M (1 : Matrix (Fin n √ó _) (Fin n √ó _) _))
```
The actual `___Map` types that we define are always linear.
```
structure PTPMap (dIn) (dOut) where
  map_mat : Matrix (dOut √ó dOut) (dIn √ó dIn) ‚ÑÇ
  pos : map_mat.IsPositiveMap
  trace_preserving : map_mat.IsTracePreserving

structure CPTPMap (dIn) (dOut) extends PTPMap dIn dOut where
  completely_pos : map_mat.IsCompletelyPositive
  pos := completely_pos.IsPositiveMap
```
### Choi Matrices
* Choi matrix of a channel:
```
def choi (Œõ : CPTPMap dIn dOut) := PTPMap.choi_matrix Œõ.map_mat
```
* Build a channel from a PSD Choi matrix with the correct trace:
```
def CPTP_of_choi_PSD_Tr {M : Matrix (dIn √ó dOut) (dIn √ó dOut) ‚ÑÇ} (h‚ÇÅ : M.PosSemidef) (h‚ÇÇ : M.trace = (Finset.univ (Œ± := dIn)).card) : CPTPMap dIn dOut
```
* Choi's theorem on CPTP maps, given as the state-channel correspondence: a channel from type `dIn` to `dOut` is equivalent to the mixed states on `dIn √ó dOut`.
```
def choi_MState_iff_CPTP (M : Matrix (dIn √ó dOut) (dIn √ó dOut) ‚ÑÇ) :
    CPTPMap dIn dOut ‚âÉ MState (dIn √ó dOut)
```
* `CPTPMap.id : CPTPMap dIn dIn`: The identity channel on Hilbert spaces of dimension `dIn`.

## Matrix Norms and Fidelities
* `Matrix.traceNorm [RCLike ùïú] (A : Matrix m n ùïú) : ‚Ñù `: The trace norm of a (potentially rectangular) matrix, as `Tr[‚àö(A‚Ä† A)]`.
* `Fidelity (œÅ œÉ : MState d) : ‚Ñù`: The fidelity between two mixed states. `Fidelity.prob (œÅ œÉ : MState d) : Prob` gives this bundled with the information that is between 0 and 1.
* `TrDistance (œÅ œÉ : MState d) : ‚Ñù`: The trace distance between two states, as half the trace norm of their difference. Also supports `TrDistance.prob`.

## Entropy
* `H‚ÇÅ : Prob ‚Üí ‚Ñù := fun x ‚Ü¶ -x * Real.log x`: the one-event entropy function.
* `H‚Çõ (d : Distribution Œ±) : ‚Ñù`: the Shannon entropy of a distribution.
* `S·µ•‚Çô (œÅ : MState d) : ‚Ñù`: the von Neumann entropy of a mixed state.
* `QConditionalEnt (œÅ : MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ)) : ‚Ñù`: Quantum Conditional Entropy, S(œÅ·¥¨|œÅ·¥Æ) = S(œÅ·¥¨·¥Æ) - S(œÅ·¥Æ)
* `QMutualInfo (œÅ : MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ)) : ‚Ñù`: Quantum Mutual Information, I(A:B) = S(œÅ·¥¨) + S(œÅ·¥Æ) - S(œÅ·¥¨·¥Æ)
* `CoherentInfo (œÅ : MState d‚ÇÅ) (Œõ : CPTPMap d‚ÇÅ d‚ÇÇ) : ‚Ñù`: Coherent information of `œÅ` under the channel `Œõ`.
* `QRelativeEnt (œÅ œÉ : MState d) : ‚Ñù`: Quantum Relative Entropy, S(œÅ‚ÄñœÉ) = Tr[œÅ (log œÅ - log œÉ)].
* `QCMI (œÅ : MState (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ √ó d‚ÇÉ)) : ‚Ñù`: Quantum Conditional Mutual Information, I(A;C|B) = S(A|B) - S(A|BC)

## `Mixable`
The `Mixable` typeclass defines a certain notion of convexity. `Convex` is for sets; `Mixable T` says that a type `T` can be cast injectively to some underlying type `U`, and the image forms a convex subset on `U` that can be then cast back to `T`. Important instances:
 * `Prob` are mixable where `U = ‚Ñù`. Probabilities are a convex subset of `‚Ñù`.
 * `Distribution d` are mixable as `d`-dimensional vectors in `‚Ñù`, that is, `d ‚Üí ‚Ñù`.
 * Quantum mixed states `MState d` are mixable as `Matrix d d ‚ÑÇ`.
 * Quantum channels `CPTPMap d‚ÇÅ d‚ÇÇ` are mixable as their Choi matrices, `Matrix (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ) (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ) ‚ÑÇ`. This is actually equivalent to the `MState` instances above through the state-channel correspondence.

You might ask, why we need to define `Mixable` at all when `Convex` already exists? Well, we want to make statements like "quantum mixed states are convex". The standard notion of convexity says that this means `p * x + (1-p) * y` is also a quantum mixed state whenver `x` and `y` are. But there's no automatic notion of what it means to add or scale quantum states, unless we want them to automatically cast back to matrices. We don't really want notation like `2 * œÅ`. Similarly, probabilities cannot in general be added (because there is no meaningful way to add the probabilities 0.5 and 0.7 to get another probability). Mixable gives a clean way of talking about them.
```

## File: QuantumInfo/Finite/Braket.lean
```
import QuantumInfo.ForMathlib
import ClassicalInfo.Distribution

/-!
Finite dimensional quantum pure states, bra and kets. Mixed states are `MState` in that file.

These could be done with a Hilbert space of Fintype, which would look like
```lean4
(H : Type*) [NormedAddCommGroup H] [InnerProductSpace ‚ÑÇ H] [CompleteSpace H] [FiniteDimensional ‚ÑÇ H]
```
or by choosing a particular `Basis` and asserting it is `Fintype`. But frankly it seems easier to
mostly focus on the basis-dependent notion of `Matrix`, which has the added benefit of an obvious
"classical" interpretation (as the basis elements, or diagonal elements of a mixed state). In that
sense, this quantum theory comes with the a particular classical theory always preferred.
-/

noncomputable section

open Classical
open BigOperators
open ComplexConjugate
open Kronecker
open scoped Matrix ComplexOrder

section
variable (d : Type*) [Fintype d]

/-- A ket as a vector of unit norm. We follow the convention in `Matrix` of vectors as simple functions
 from a Fintype. Kets are distinctly not a vector space in our notion, as they represent only normalized
 states and so cannot (in general) be added or scaled. -/
structure Ket where
  vec : d ‚Üí ‚ÑÇ
  normalized' : ‚àë x, ‚Äñvec x‚Äñ ^ 2 = 1
  --TODO: change to `vec : EuclideanSpace ‚ÑÇ d` / `normalized' : ‚Äñvec‚Äñ = 1`

/-- A bra is identical in definition to a `Ket`, but are separate to avoid complex conjugation confusion.
 They can be interconverted with the adjoint: `Ket.to_bra` and `Bra.to_ket` -/
structure Bra where
  vec : d ‚Üí ‚ÑÇ
  normalized' : ‚àë x, ‚Äñvec x‚Äñ ^ 2 =1

end section

namespace Braket

scoped notation:max "„Äà" œà:90 "‚à£" => (œà : Bra _)

scoped notation:max "‚à£" œà:90 "„Äâ" => (œà : Ket _)

variable {d : Type*} [Fintype d]

instance instFunLikeKet : FunLike (Ket d) d ‚ÑÇ where
  coe œà := œà.vec
  coe_injective' _ _ h := by rwa [Ket.mk.injEq]

instance instFunLikeBra : FunLike (Bra d) d ‚ÑÇ where
  coe œà := œà.vec
  coe_injective' _ _ h := by rwa [Bra.mk.injEq]

def dot (Œæ : Bra d) (œà : Ket d) : ‚ÑÇ := ‚àë x, (Œæ x) * (œà x)

scoped notation "„Äà" Œæ:90 "‚Äñ" œà:90 "„Äâ" => dot (Œæ : Bra _) (œà : Ket _)

end Braket

section braket
open Braket

variable {d : Type*} [Fintype d]

theorem Ket.apply (œà : Ket d) (i : d) : œà i = œà.vec i :=
  rfl

theorem Bra.apply (œà : Bra d) (i : d) : œà i = œà.vec i :=
  rfl

@[ext]
theorem Ket.ext {Œæ œà : Ket d} (h : ‚àÄ x, Œæ x = œà x) : Œæ = œà :=
  DFunLike.ext Œæ œà h

@[ext]
theorem Bra.ext {Œæ œà : Bra d} (h : ‚àÄ x, Œæ x = œà x) : Œæ = œà :=
  DFunLike.ext Œæ œà h

theorem Ket.normalized (œà : Ket d) : ‚àë x, Complex.normSq (œà x) = 1 := by
  convert œà.normalized'
  rw [Complex.normSq_eq_norm_sq]
  rfl

theorem Bra.normalized (œà : Bra d) : ‚àë x, Complex.normSq (œà x) = 1 := by
  convert œà.normalized'
  rw [Complex.normSq_eq_norm_sq]
  rfl

/-- Any Bra can be turned into a Ket by conjugating the elements. -/
@[coe]
def Ket.to_bra (œà : Ket d) : Bra d :=
  ‚ü®conj œà, by simpa using œà.2‚ü©

/-- Any Ket can be turned into a Bra by conjugating the elements. -/
@[coe]
def Bra.to_ket (œà : Bra d) : Ket d :=
  ‚ü®conj œà, by simpa using œà.2‚ü©

instance instBraOfKet : Coe (Ket d) (Bra d) := ‚ü®Ket.to_bra‚ü©

instance instKetOfBra : Coe (Bra d) (Ket d) := ‚ü®Bra.to_ket‚ü©

@[simp]
theorem Bra.eq_conj (œà : Ket d) (x : d) :„Äàœà‚à£ x = conj (‚à£œà„Äâ x) :=
  rfl

theorem Bra.apply' (œà : Ket d) (i : d) : „Äàœà‚à£ i = conj (œà.vec i) :=
  rfl

theorem Ket.exists_ne_zero (œà : Ket d) : ‚àÉ x, œà x ‚â† 0 := by
  have hzerolt : ‚àë x : d, Complex.normSq (œà x) > ‚àë x : d, 0 := by rw [œà.normalized, Finset.sum_const_zero]; exact zero_lt_one
  have hpos : ‚àÉ x ‚àà Finset.univ, 0 < Complex.normSq (œà x) := Finset.exists_lt_of_sum_lt hzerolt
  obtain ‚ü®x, _, hpos‚ü© := hpos
  rw [Complex.normSq_pos] at hpos
  use x

theorem Bra.exists_ne_zero (œà : Bra d) : ‚àÉ x, œà x ‚â† 0 := by
  have hzerolt : ‚àë x : d, Complex.normSq (œà x) > ‚àë x : d, 0 := by rw [œà.normalized, Finset.sum_const_zero]; exact zero_lt_one
  have hpos : ‚àÉ x ‚àà Finset.univ, 0 < Complex.normSq (œà x) := Finset.exists_lt_of_sum_lt hzerolt
  obtain ‚ü®x, _, hpos‚ü© := hpos
  rw [Complex.normSq_pos] at hpos
  use x

/-- Create a ket out of a vector given it has a nonzero component -/
def Ket.normalize (v : d ‚Üí ‚ÑÇ) (h : ‚àÉ x, v x ‚â† 0) : Ket d :=
  { vec := fun x ‚Ü¶ v x / ‚àö(‚àë x : d, ‚Äñv x‚Äñ ^ 2),
    normalized' := by
      simp only [‚Üê Complex.normSq_eq_norm_sq, Complex.normSq_div,
        Complex.normSq_ofReal, ‚Üêsq]
      have hnonneg : ‚àë x : d, Complex.normSq (v x) ‚â• 0 := Fintype.sum_nonneg (fun x => Complex.normSq_nonneg (v x))
      simp only [Real.sq_sqrt hnonneg, div_eq_inv_mul, ‚ÜêFinset.mul_sum]
      apply inv_mul_cancel‚ÇÄ
      by_contra hzero
      rw [Fintype.sum_eq_zero_iff_of_nonneg (fun x => Complex.normSq_nonneg (v x))] at hzero
      obtain ‚ü®a, ha‚ü© := h
      have h‚ÇÅ : (fun x => Complex.normSq (v x)) a ‚â† 0 := by simp only [ne_eq, map_eq_zero]; exact ha
      exact h‚ÇÅ (congrFun hzero a)
  }

/-- A ket is already normalized -/
theorem Ket.normalize_ket_eq_self (œà : Ket d) : Ket.normalize (œà.vec) (Ket.exists_ne_zero œà) = œà := by
  ext x
  unfold normalize
  simp only [apply, œà.normalized', Real.sqrt_one, Complex.ofReal_one, div_one]

/-- Create a bra out of a vector given it has a nonzero component -/
def Bra.normalize (v : d ‚Üí ‚ÑÇ) (h : ‚àÉ x, v x ‚â† 0) : Bra d :=
  { vec := fun x ‚Ü¶ v x / ‚àö(‚àë x : d, ‚Äñv x‚Äñ ^ 2),
    normalized' := by
      simp only [‚Üê Complex.normSq_eq_norm_sq, Complex.normSq_div,
      Complex.normSq_ofReal, ‚Üêsq]
      have hnonneg : ‚àë x : d, Complex.normSq (v x) ‚â• 0 := Fintype.sum_nonneg (fun x => Complex.normSq_nonneg (v x))
      simp only [Real.sq_sqrt hnonneg, div_eq_inv_mul, ‚ÜêFinset.mul_sum]
      apply inv_mul_cancel‚ÇÄ
      by_contra hzero
      rw [Fintype.sum_eq_zero_iff_of_nonneg (fun x => Complex.normSq_nonneg (v x))] at hzero
      obtain ‚ü®a, ha‚ü© := h
      have h‚ÇÅ : (fun x => Complex.normSq (v x)) a ‚â† 0 := by simp only [ne_eq, map_eq_zero]; exact ha
      exact h‚ÇÅ (congrFun hzero a)
  }

/-- A bra is already normalized -/
def Bra.normalize_ket_eq_self (œà : Bra d) : Bra.normalize (œà.vec) (Bra.exists_ne_zero œà) = œà := by
  ext x
  unfold normalize
  simp only [apply, œà.normalized', Real.sqrt_one, Complex.ofReal_one, div_one]

/-- Ket form by the superposition of all elements in `d`.
Commonly denoted by |+‚ü©, especially for qubits -/
def uniform_superposition [hdne : Nonempty d] : Ket d := by
  let f : d ‚Üí ‚ÑÇ := fun _ ‚Ü¶ 1
  have hfnezero : ‚àÉ x, f x ‚â† 0 := by
    obtain ‚ü®i‚ü© := hdne
    use i
    simp only [f, ne_eq, one_ne_zero, not_false_eq_true]
  exact Ket.normalize f hfnezero

/-- There exists a ket for every nonempty `d`.
Here, we use the uniform superposition -/
instance instInhabited [Nonempty d] : Inhabited (Ket d) where
  default := uniform_superposition

/-- Construct the Ket corresponding to a basis vector, with a +1 phase. -/
def Ket.basis (i : d) : Ket d :=
  ‚ü®fun j ‚Ü¶ if i = j then 1 else 0, by simp [apply_ite]‚ü©

/-- Construct the Bra corresponding to a basis vector, with a +1 phase. -/
def Bra.basis (i : d) : Bra d :=
  ‚ü®fun j ‚Ü¶ if i = j then 1 else 0, by simp [apply_ite]‚ü©

/-- A Bra can be viewed as a function from Ket's to ‚ÑÇ. -/
instance instFunLikeBraket : FunLike (Bra d) (Ket d) ‚ÑÇ where
  coe Œæ := dot Œæ
  coe_injective' x y h := by
    ext i
    simpa [Ket.basis, dot, Ket.apply] using congrFun h (Ket.basis i)

/-- The inner product of any state with itself is 1. -/
theorem Braket.dot_self_eq_one (œà : Ket d) :„Äàœà‚Äñœà„Äâ= 1 := by
  have h‚ÇÅ : ‚àÄx, conj (œà x) * œà x = Complex.normSq (œà x) := fun x ‚Ü¶ by
    rw [Complex.normSq_eq_conj_mul_self]
  simp only [dot, Bra.eq_conj, h‚ÇÅ]
  have h‚ÇÇ := congrArg Complex.ofReal œà.normalized
  simpa using h‚ÇÇ

section prod
variable {d d‚ÇÅ d‚ÇÇ : Type*} [Fintype d] [Fintype d‚ÇÅ] [Fintype d‚ÇÇ]

/-- The outer product of two kets, creating an unentangled state. -/
def Ket.prod (œà‚ÇÅ : Ket d‚ÇÅ) (œà‚ÇÇ : Ket d‚ÇÇ) : Ket (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ) where
  vec := fun (i,j) ‚Ü¶ œà‚ÇÅ i * œà‚ÇÇ j
  normalized' := by
    simp only [Fintype.sum_prod_type, norm_mul, ‚Üê Complex.normSq_eq_norm_sq, mul_pow,
      ‚Üê Finset.mul_sum, œà‚ÇÇ.normalized, mul_one, œà‚ÇÅ.normalized]

infixl:100 " ‚äó " => Ket.prod

/-- A Ket is a product if it's `Ket.prod` of two kets. -/
def Ket.IsProd (œà : Ket (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ)) : Prop := ‚àÉ Œæ œÜ, œà = Œæ ‚äó œÜ

/-- A Ket is entangled if it's not `Ket.prod` of two kets. -/
def Ket.IsEntangled (œà : Ket (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ)) : Prop := ¬¨œà.IsProd

/-- `Ket.prod` states are product states. -/
@[simp]
theorem Ket.IsProd_prod (œà‚ÇÅ : Ket d‚ÇÅ) (œà‚ÇÇ : Ket d‚ÇÇ) : (œà‚ÇÅ.prod œà‚ÇÇ).IsProd :=
  ‚ü®œà‚ÇÅ, œà‚ÇÇ, rfl‚ü©

/-- `Ket.prod` states are not entangled states. -/
@[simp]
theorem Ket.not_IsEntangled_prod (œà‚ÇÅ : Ket d‚ÇÅ) (œà‚ÇÇ : Ket d‚ÇÇ) : ¬¨(œà‚ÇÅ.prod œà‚ÇÇ).IsEntangled :=
  (¬∑ (œà‚ÇÅ.IsProd_prod œà‚ÇÇ))

/-- A ket is a product state iff its components are cross-multiplicative. -/
theorem Ket.IsProd_iff_mul_eq_mul (œà : Ket (d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ)) : œà.IsProd ‚Üî
    ‚àÄ i‚ÇÅ i‚ÇÇ j‚ÇÅ j‚ÇÇ, œà (i‚ÇÅ,j‚ÇÅ)  * œà (i‚ÇÇ,j‚ÇÇ) = œà (i‚ÇÅ,j‚ÇÇ) * œà (i‚ÇÇ,j‚ÇÅ) := by
  constructor
  ¬∑ rintro ‚ü®Œæ,œÜ,rfl‚ü© i‚ÇÅ i‚ÇÇ j‚ÇÅ j‚ÇÇ
    simp only [prod, apply]
    ring_nf
  ¬∑ intro hcrossm
    obtain ‚ü®‚ü®a, b‚ü©, hœànonZero‚ü© := Ket.exists_ne_zero œà
    -- May be able to simplify proof below by using Ket.normalize
    let v‚ÇÅ : d‚ÇÅ ‚Üí ‚ÑÇ := fun x => ‚Äñœà (a, b)‚Äñ / (œà (a, b)) * ((œà (x, b)) / ‚àö(‚àë i : d‚ÇÅ, ‚Äñœà (i, b)‚Äñ^2))
    let v‚ÇÇ : d‚ÇÇ ‚Üí ‚ÑÇ := fun y => œà (a, y) / ‚àö(‚àë j : d‚ÇÇ, ‚Äñœà (a, j)‚Äñ^2)
    have hv1Norm : ‚àë x, ‚Äñv‚ÇÅ x‚Äñ^2 = 1 := by
      simp only [‚Üê Complex.normSq_eq_norm_sq, v‚ÇÅ, Complex.normSq_mul, Complex.normSq_div,
      Complex.normSq_ofReal, ‚Üê sq]
      rw [div_self _]
      have hnonneg : ‚àë i : d‚ÇÅ, Complex.normSq (œà (i, b)) ‚â• 0 := Fintype.sum_nonneg (fun i => Complex.normSq_nonneg (œà (i, b)))
      ¬∑ simp_rw [Real.sq_sqrt hnonneg, one_mul, div_eq_inv_mul, ‚ÜêFinset.mul_sum]
        apply inv_mul_cancel‚ÇÄ
        by_contra hzero
        rw [Fintype.sum_eq_zero_iff_of_nonneg (fun i => Complex.normSq_nonneg (œà (i, b)))] at hzero
        have h‚ÇÅ : (fun i => Complex.normSq (œà (i,b))) a ‚â† 0 := by simp only [ne_eq, map_eq_zero]; exact hœànonZero
        rw [hzero, Pi.zero_apply, ne_eq, eq_self, not_true_eq_false] at h‚ÇÅ
        exact h‚ÇÅ
      ¬∑ simp_all only [ne_eq, map_eq_zero, not_false_eq_true]
    have hv2Norm : ‚àë x, ‚Äñv‚ÇÇ x‚Äñ^2 = 1 := by
      simp only [‚Üê Complex.normSq_eq_norm_sq, v‚ÇÇ, Complex.normSq_div,
      Complex.normSq_ofReal, ‚Üê sq]
      have hnonneg : ‚àë j : d‚ÇÇ, Complex.normSq (œà (a, j)) ‚â• 0 := Fintype.sum_nonneg (fun j => Complex.normSq_nonneg (œà (a, j)))
      simp_rw [Real.sq_sqrt hnonneg, div_eq_inv_mul, ‚ÜêFinset.mul_sum]
      apply inv_mul_cancel‚ÇÄ
      by_contra hzero
      rw [Fintype.sum_eq_zero_iff_of_nonneg (fun j => Complex.normSq_nonneg (œà (a, j)))] at hzero
      have h‚ÇÅ : (fun j => Complex.normSq (œà (a, j))) b ‚â† 0 := by simp only [ne_eq, map_eq_zero]; exact hœànonZero
      rw [hzero, Pi.zero_apply, ne_eq, eq_self, not_true_eq_false] at h‚ÇÅ
      exact h‚ÇÅ
    let œà‚ÇÅ : Ket d‚ÇÅ := ‚ü®v‚ÇÅ, hv1Norm‚ü©
    let œà‚ÇÇ : Ket d‚ÇÇ := ‚ü®v‚ÇÇ, hv2Norm‚ü©
    use œà‚ÇÅ, œà‚ÇÇ
    ext ‚ü®x, y‚ü©
    have hœàfun : œà (x, y) = (œà (x, b) * œà (a, y)) / œà (a, b) := eq_div_of_mul_eq hœànonZero (hcrossm x a y b)
    have hœànorm : (‚àë z : d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ, Complex.normSq (œà.vec (z.1, b) * œà.vec (a, z.2))) = Complex.normSq (œà (a, b)) :=
    calc
      ‚àë z : d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ, Complex.normSq (œà.vec (z.1, b) * œà.vec (a, z.2)) =
        ‚àë z : d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ, Complex.normSq (œà.vec (a, b) * œà.vec (z.1, z.2)) := by simp only [‚Üê apply, hcrossm, mul_comm]
      _ = ‚àë z : d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ, Complex.normSq (œà.vec (a, b)) * Complex.normSq (œà.vec (z.1, z.2)) := by simp only [Complex.normSq_mul]
      _ = Complex.normSq (œà.vec (a, b)) * ‚àë z : d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ, Complex.normSq (œà.vec z) := by rw [‚ÜêFinset.mul_sum]
      _ = Complex.normSq (œà.vec (a, b)) := by simp only [‚Üê apply, œà.normalized, mul_one]
    simp [prod, apply, œà‚ÇÅ, œà‚ÇÇ, v‚ÇÅ, v‚ÇÇ]
    rw [mul_assoc, ‚Üêmul_div_mul_comm, ‚ÜêComplex.ofReal_mul, ‚ÜêReal.sqrt_mul (Finset.sum_nonneg _)]
    ¬∑
      simp_rw [Fintype.sum_mul_sum, ‚ÜêFintype.sum_prod_type']
      simp only [‚Üê Complex.normSq_eq_norm_sq]
      simp_rw [Fintype.sum_congr _ _ (fun z : d‚ÇÅ √ó d‚ÇÇ => (Complex.normSq_mul (œà.vec (z.1, b)) (œà.vec (a, z.2))).symm)]
      simp_rw [hœànorm, Complex.normSq_eq_norm_sq, Real.sqrt_sq_eq_abs, abs_norm, apply]
      ring_nf
      rw [mul_comm, ‚Üêmul_assoc, ‚Üêmul_assoc, ‚Üêmul_assoc]
      nth_rw 2 [‚Üêinv_inv (Complex.ofReal (‚Äñœà.vec (a, b)‚Äñ))]
      rw [Complex.mul_inv_cancel _]
      ¬∑ rw [one_mul]
        ring_nf at hœàfun
        simp_rw [Ket.apply, mul_comm, mul_comm (œà.vec (a, y)) _, ‚Üêmul_assoc] at hœàfun
        exact hœàfun
      ¬∑ simp_all [Ket.apply]
    ¬∑ simp
end prod

section mes
/-- The Maximally Entangled State, or MES, on a d√ód system. In principle there are many, this
is specifically the MES with an all-positive phase. For instance on `d := Fin 2`, this is the
Bell state. -/
def Ket.MES (d) [Fintype d] [Nonempty d] : Ket (d √ó d) where
  vec := fun (i,j) ‚Ü¶ if i = j then 1 / Real.sqrt (Fintype.card (Œ± := d)) else 0
  normalized' := by
    simp [apply_ite, Fintype.sum_prod_type]

/-- On any space of dimension at least two, the maximally entangled state `MES` is entangled. -/
theorem Ket.MES_isEntangled [Nontrivial d] : (Ket.MES d).IsEntangled := by
  obtain ‚ü®x, y, h‚ü© := @Nontrivial.exists_pair_ne d _
  rw [IsEntangled, MES, IsProd_iff_mul_eq_mul]
  push_neg
  use x, y, x, y
  simp [apply, h]

end mes

section equiv

/-- The equivalence relation on `Ket` where two kets equivalent if they are equal up to a global phase, i.e. `‚àÉ z, ‚Äñz‚Äñ = 1 ‚àß a.vec = z ‚Ä¢ b.vec -/
def Ket.PhaseEquiv : Setoid (Ket d) where
  r a b := ‚àÉ z : ‚ÑÇ, ‚Äñz‚Äñ = 1 ‚àß a.vec = z ‚Ä¢ b.vec
  iseqv := {
    refl := fun x ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®1, by simp‚ü©,
    symm := fun ‚ü®z,h‚ÇÅ,h‚ÇÇ‚ü© ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®conj z,
      by simp [h‚ÇÅ],
      by simp [h‚ÇÅ, h‚ÇÇ, smul_smul, ‚Üê Complex.normSq_eq_conj_mul_self, Complex.normSq_eq_norm_sq]‚ü©,
    trans := fun ‚ü®z‚ÇÅ,h‚ÇÅ‚ÇÅ,h‚ÇÅ‚ÇÇ‚ü© ‚ü®z‚ÇÇ,h‚ÇÇ‚ÇÅ,h‚ÇÇ‚ÇÇ‚ü© ‚Ü¶ ‚ü®z‚ÇÅ * z‚ÇÇ,
      by simp [h‚ÇÅ‚ÇÅ, h‚ÇÇ‚ÇÅ],
      by simp [h‚ÇÅ‚ÇÇ, h‚ÇÇ‚ÇÇ, smul_smul]‚ü©
  }

variable (d) in
/-- The type of `Ket`s up to a global phase equivalence, as given by `Ket.PhaseEquiv`. In particular, `MState`s really only care about a KetUpToPhase, and not Kets themselves. -/
def KetUpToPhase :=
  @Quotient (Ket d) Ket.PhaseEquiv

end equiv
end braket

```

## File: QuantumInfo/Finite/CPTPMap/Bundled.lean
```
import QuantumInfo.Finite.CPTPMap.Unbundled
import QuantumInfo.Finite.MState

import Mathlib.Topology.Order.Hom.Basic

/-! # Classes of Matrix Maps

The bundled `MatrixMap`s: `HPMap`, `UnitalMap`, `TPMap`, `PMap`, and `CPMap`.
These are defined over the bare minimum rings (`Semiring` or `RCLike`, respectively).

The combinations `PTPMap` (positive trace-preserving), `CPTPMap`, and `CPUMap`
(CP unital maps) take ‚ÑÇ as the default class.

The majority of quantum theory revolves around `CPTPMap`s, so those are explored more
thoroughly in their file CPTP.lean.
-/

--PULLOUT
open ComplexOrder in
theorem Matrix.PosSemidef.trace_pos {n ùïú : Type*} [Fintype n] [RCLike ùïú]
    {A : Matrix n n ùïú} (hA : A.PosSemidef) (h : A ‚â† 0) : 0 < A.trace := by
  classical
  apply hA.trace_nonneg.lt_of_ne'
  rw [hA.left.trace_eq_sum_eigenvalues]
  suffices ‚àë i, hA.left.eigenvalues i ‚â† 0 from mod_cast this
  rwa [ne_eq, Fintype.sum_eq_zero_iff_of_nonneg hA.eigenvalues_nonneg,
    hA.left.eigenvalues_eq_zero_iff]

--PULLOUT
open ComplexOrder in
theorem HermitianMat.trace_pos {n ùïú : Type*} [Fintype n] [RCLike ùïú]
    {A : HermitianMat n ùïú} (hA : 0 < A) : 0 < A.trace := by
  have hA' := hA.le
  rw [HermitianMat.zero_le_iff] at hA'
  have h_pos := Matrix.PosSemidef.trace_pos hA' (by simpa using hA.ne')
  rw [HermitianMat.trace_eq_re_trace]
  rw [RCLike.pos_iff] at h_pos
  exact h_pos.left

variable (dIn dOut R : Type*) (ùïú : Type := ‚ÑÇ)
variable [Fintype dIn] [Fintype dOut]
variable [Semiring R] [RCLike ùïú]

/-- Hermitian-preserving linear maps. -/
structure HPMap extends MatrixMap dIn dOut ùïú where
  HP : MatrixMap.IsHermitianPreserving toLinearMap

/-- Unital linear maps. -/
structure UnitalMap [DecidableEq dIn] [DecidableEq dOut] extends MatrixMap dIn dOut R where
  unital : MatrixMap.Unital toLinearMap

/-- Trace-preserving linear maps. -/
structure TPMap extends MatrixMap dIn dOut R where
  TP : MatrixMap.IsTracePreserving toLinearMap

--Mark this as [simp] so that simp lemmas requiring `IsTracePreserving` can pick it up.
--In theory this could be making "IsTracePreserving" a typeclass ... or more realistically,
--defining a `TracePreservingClass` similar to `AddHomClass`
attribute [simp] TPMap.TP

/-- Positive linear maps. -/
structure PMap extends HPMap dIn dOut ùïú where
  pos : MatrixMap.IsPositive toLinearMap
  HP := pos.IsHermitianPreserving

/-- Completely positive linear maps. -/
structure CPMap [DecidableEq dIn] extends PMap dIn dOut ùïú where
  cp : MatrixMap.IsCompletelyPositive toLinearMap
  pos := cp.IsPositive

/-- Positive trace-preserving linear maps. These includes all channels, but aren't
  necessarily *completely* positive, see `CPTPMap`. -/
structure PTPMap extends PMap dIn dOut ùïú, TPMap dIn dOut ùïú

/-- Positive unital maps. These are important because they are the
  dual to `PTPMap`: they are the most general way to map *observables*. -/
structure PUMap [DecidableEq dIn] [DecidableEq dOut] extends PMap dIn dOut ùïú, UnitalMap dIn dOut ùïú

attribute [simp] PTPMap.TP

/-- Completely positive trace-preserving linear maps. This is the most common
  meaning of "channel", often described as "the most general physically realizable
  quantum operation". -/
structure CPTPMap [DecidableEq dIn] extends PTPMap dIn dOut (ùïú := ùïú), CPMap dIn dOut ùïú where

/-- Completely positive unital maps. These are important because they are the
  dual to `CPTPMap`: they are the physically realizable ways to map *observables*. -/
structure CPUMap [DecidableEq dIn] [DecidableEq dOut] extends CPMap dIn dOut ùïú, PUMap dIn dOut ùïú

variable {dIn dOut R} {ùïú : Type} [RCLike ùïú]

--Hermitian-presering maps: continuous linear maps on HermitianMats.
namespace HPMap
omit [Fintype dIn] [Fintype dOut]
variable {Œõ‚ÇÅ Œõ‚ÇÇ : HPMap dIn dOut ùïú}
variable {CŒõ‚ÇÅ CŒõ‚ÇÇ : HPMap dIn dOut ‚ÑÇ}

abbrev map (M : HPMap dIn dOut ùïú) : MatrixMap dIn dOut ùïú := M.toLinearMap

@[ext]
theorem ext (h : Œõ‚ÇÅ.map = Œõ‚ÇÇ.map) : Œõ‚ÇÅ = Œõ‚ÇÇ := by
  rwa [HPMap.mk.injEq]

/-- Two maps are equal if they agree on all Hermitian inputs. -/
theorem funext_hermitian (h : ‚àÄ M : HermitianMat dIn ‚ÑÇ, CŒõ‚ÇÅ.map M = CŒõ‚ÇÇ.map M) :
    CŒõ‚ÇÅ = CŒõ‚ÇÇ := by
  ext M : 2
  have hH := h (realPart M)
  have hA := h (imaginaryPart M)
  convert congr($hH + Complex.I ‚Ä¢ $hA)
  <;> rw (occs := [1]) [‚Üê realPart_add_I_smul_imaginaryPart M, map_add, map_smul]


/-- Two maps are equal if they agree on all positive inputs. -/
theorem funext_pos [Fintype dIn] (h : ‚àÄ M : HermitianMat dIn ‚ÑÇ, 0 ‚â§ M ‚Üí CŒõ‚ÇÅ.map M = CŒõ‚ÇÇ.map M) :
    CŒõ‚ÇÅ = CŒõ‚ÇÇ := by
  classical
  open scoped HermitianMat in
  apply funext_hermitian
  intro M
  have hPos := h M‚Å∫ M.zero_le_posPart
  have hNeg := h M‚Åª M.negPart_le_zero --TODO: this is named incorrectly
  rw [‚Üê M.posPart_add_negPart]
  simp [hPos, hNeg]

/-- Two maps are equal if they agree on all positive inputs with trace one -/
theorem funext_pos_trace [Fintype dIn]
  (h : ‚àÄ M : HermitianMat dIn ‚ÑÇ, 0 ‚â§ M ‚Üí M.trace = 1 ‚Üí CŒõ‚ÇÅ.map M = CŒõ‚ÇÇ.map M) :
    CŒõ‚ÇÅ = CŒõ‚ÇÇ := by
  apply funext_pos
  intro M hM'
  rcases hM'.eq_or_lt with rfl | hM
  ¬∑ simp
  have h_tr : 0 < M.trace := M.trace_pos hM
  have := h (M.trace‚Åª¬π ‚Ä¢ M) ?_ ?_
  ¬∑ simp only [selfAdjoint.val_smul, LinearMap.map_smul_of_tower] at this
    convert congr(M.trace ‚Ä¢ $this)
    ¬∑ rw [smul_smul]
      field_simp
      simp
    ¬∑ rw [smul_smul]
      field_simp
      simp
  ¬∑ apply smul_nonneg (by positivity) hM'
  ¬∑ simp [field]

/-- Two maps are equal if they agree on all `MState`s. -/
theorem funext_mstate [Fintype dIn] [DecidableEq dIn] {Œõ‚ÇÅ Œõ‚ÇÇ : HPMap dIn dOut ‚ÑÇ}
  (h : ‚àÄ œÅ : MState dIn, Œõ‚ÇÅ.map œÅ.m = Œõ‚ÇÇ.map œÅ.m) :
    Œõ‚ÇÅ = Œõ‚ÇÇ :=
  funext_pos_trace fun M hM_pos hM_tr ‚Ü¶ h ‚ü®M, hM_pos, hM_tr‚ü©

/-- Hermitian-preserving maps are functions from `HermitianMat`s to `HermitianMat`s. -/
instance instFunLike : FunLike (HPMap dIn dOut ‚ÑÇ) (HermitianMat dIn ‚ÑÇ) (HermitianMat dOut ‚ÑÇ) where
  coe Œõ œÅ := ‚ü®Œõ.map œÅ.1, Œõ.HP œÅ.2‚ü©
  coe_injective' x y h := funext_hermitian fun M ‚Ü¶
    by simpa using congrFun h M

instance : ContinuousLinearMapClass
    (HPMap dIn dOut ‚ÑÇ) ‚Ñù (HermitianMat dIn ‚ÑÇ) (HermitianMat dOut ‚ÑÇ) where
  map_add f x y := HermitianMat.ext <| LinearMap.map_add f.toLinearMap x y
  map_smul‚Çõ‚Çó f c x := HermitianMat.ext <| by simp [instFunLike]
  map_continuous f := .subtype_mk (by fun_prop) _

end HPMap

--Positive-preserving maps: continuous linear order-preserving maps on HermitianMats.
namespace PMap

@[ext]
theorem ext {Œõ‚ÇÅ Œõ‚ÇÇ : PMap dIn dOut ùïú} (h : Œõ‚ÇÅ.map = Œõ‚ÇÇ.map) : Œõ‚ÇÅ = Œõ‚ÇÇ := by
  rw [PMap.mk.injEq]
  exact HPMap.ext h

theorem injective_toHPMap : (PMap.toHPMap (dIn := dIn) (dOut := dOut) (ùïú := ùïú)).Injective :=
  fun _ _ ‚Ü¶ (mk.injEq _ _ _ _).mpr

/-- Positive maps are functions from `HermitianMat`s to `HermitianMat`s. -/
instance instFunLike : FunLike (PMap dIn dOut ‚ÑÇ) (HermitianMat dIn ‚ÑÇ) (HermitianMat dOut ‚ÑÇ) where
  coe := DFunLike.coe ‚àò toHPMap
  coe_injective' := DFunLike.coe_injective'.comp injective_toHPMap

set_option synthInstance.maxHeartbeats 40000 in

  map_add f x y := HermitianMat.ext <| LinearMap.map_add f.toLinearMap x y
  map_smul‚Çõ‚Çó f c x := HermitianMat.ext <| by simp [instFunLike]

instance instContinuousOrderHomClass : ContinuousOrderHomClass (PMap dIn dOut ‚ÑÇ)
    (HermitianMat dIn ‚ÑÇ) (HermitianMat dOut ‚ÑÇ) where
  map_continuous f := ContinuousMapClass.map_continuous f.toHPMap
  map_monotone f x y h := by
    simpa using f.pos h

/-- Positive-presering maps also preserve positivity on, specifically, Hermitian matrices. -/
@[simp]
theorem pos_Hermitian (M : PMap dIn dOut ‚ÑÇ) {x : HermitianMat dIn ‚ÑÇ} (h : 0 ‚â§ x) : 0 ‚â§ M x := by
  simpa only [map_zero] using ContinuousOrderHomClass.map_monotone M h

end PMap

def of_kraus_CPMap {Œ∫ : Type*} [Fintype Œ∫] [DecidableEq dIn] (M : Œ∫ ‚Üí Matrix dOut dIn ùïú) : CPMap dIn dOut ùïú where
  toLinearMap := MatrixMap.of_kraus M M
  cp := MatrixMap.IsCompletelyPositive.of_kraus_isCompletelyPositive M

--Positive trace-preserving maps:

  exact PMap.ext h

  fun _ _ ‚Ü¶ (mk.injEq _ _ _ _).mpr

/-- `PTPMap`s are functions from `MState`s to `MState`s. -/
instance instMFunLike [DecidableEq dIn] [DecidableEq dOut] :
    FunLike (PTPMap dIn dOut) (MState dIn) (MState dOut) where
  coe Œõ œÅ := MState.mk
    (Œõ.toHPMap œÅ.M) (HermitianMat.zero_le_iff.mpr (Œõ.pos œÅ.pos)) (by
      rw [HermitianMat.trace_eq_one_iff, ‚Üê œÅ.tr']
      exact Œõ.TP œÅ)
  coe_injective' x y h := injective_toPMap <| PMap.injective_toHPMap <|
    HPMap.funext_mstate fun œÅ ‚Ü¶ by
      have := congr($h œÅ);
      rwa [MState.ext_iff, HermitianMat.ext_iff] at this

instance instMContinuousMapClass [DecidableEq dIn] [DecidableEq dOut] :
    ContinuousMapClass (PTPMap dIn dOut) (MState dIn) (MState dOut) where
  map_continuous f := by
    rw [continuous_induced_rng]
    exact (map_continuous f.toHPMap).comp MState.Continuous_HermitianMat

-- @[norm_cast]
theorem val_apply_MState [DecidableEq dIn] (M : PTPMap dIn dOut) (œÅ : MState dIn) :
    (M œÅ : HermitianMat dOut ‚ÑÇ) = (instFunLike.coe M) œÅ := by
  rfl

--If we have a PTPMap, the input and output dimensions are always both nonempty (otherwise
--we can't preserve trace) - or they're both empty. So `[Nonempty dIn]` will always suffice.
-- This would be nice as an `instance` but that would leave `dIn` as a metavariable.
theorem nonemptyOut (Œõ : PTPMap dIn dOut) [hIn : Nonempty dIn] [DecidableEq dIn] : Nonempty dOut := by
  by_contra h
  simp only [not_nonempty_iff] at h
  let M := (1 : Matrix dIn dIn ‚ÑÇ)
  have := calc (Finset.univ.card (Œ± := dIn) : ‚ÑÇ)
    _ = M.trace := by simp [Matrix.trace, M]
    _ = (Œõ.map M).trace := (Œõ.TP M).symm
    _ = 0 := by simp only [Matrix.trace_eq_zero_of_isEmpty]
  norm_num [Finset.univ_eq_empty_iff] at this

end PTPMap
